She was being very well behaved, thank you very much.

Chapter 1

Agatha Harkness was completely okay.

She did not break two separate wine glasses, crash into a waiter and almost stab Jen’s hand with a steak knife because she was not fine. She was totally fine.

She was being very well behaved, thank you very much.

It completely did not matter to her that she was sitting in a restaurant on what should have been a very happy day, you know, celebrating her promotion with her friends, yada yada, and that it turned into objectively the worst day when she walked in.

She being the she-devil that was hanging off Rio’s arm like she didn’t have a spine of her own and would fucking fall apart if she let Rio go.

When Rio walked in an hour ago hand in hand with the woman, Agatha admitted internally that she was pretty. She had deep red hair, long legs and a sweet smile. Agatha was ready to fist pump Rio and flirt relentlessly with her date while winking at her friends at the panic she incited. And then Rio opened her fucking mouth.

“This is my girlfriend, Natasha.” Rio smiled, looking over at the redhead shyly.

Agatha’s blood boiled.

Because Natasha’s dress was far too fucking short for the restaurant they were in and her legs were unnaturally long, like freakishly long, and she was embarrassing them all by smiling so much. She looked like an idiot. She was making them all look like idiots.

Agatha hated feeling like an idiot.

“You can call me Nat!” She said, sitting by Rio. She giggled when Rio kissed her bare shoulder.

That’s when the first glass broke.

It was because Agatha was inspecting how much force a glass could take for scientific purposes. Not because her best friend was saddling up to a girl and calling her ‘girlfriend,’ since when did Rio have girlfriends?

Rio never did committed relationships. Sure, she was sexually active and once in a while she would bring girls over to meet her friends, but they never lasted longer than a week. And no labels, certain or uncertain, were ever used.
Ever since she and Agatha met in college, she always had one foot out the door. Her parents were always at each other’s throats, the Puerto-Rican fire never fully meshing well with the Irish stubbornness. Somehow, Rio got both the responsibility of holding her parents together and their ire. But the one thing her parents stood firm on, never wavering no matter how much it was threatened, was never getting divorced even though they couldn’t look each other in the eye. So, obviously, Rio looked at relationships with the same enthusiasm that most people looked at a puppy getting kicked.

It took Agatha three months to convince her that yes, they were friends. It took a year to get her to admit they were best friends. It took filming an entire movie together, literally working side by side for six months, burning the midnight oil, fielding challenges together, seeing each other cry and fail and succeed, for Rio to admit that they knew each other inside out. And Agatha didn’t blame her. With an absent father and an overbearing mother, she had her own fair share of family-related avoidance issues to battle through.

Honestly, together, they had them all. Rio was fearful avoidant, Agatha was dismissive avoidant and together they were just avoidant and avoidant. It’s why they never dated.

That and the fact that they immediately friend-zoned each other.

“So, how did you two meet?” Jen asked Rio and Nat while a waiter cleaned up the glass from Agatha’s hand. She was lucky there was no blood. She was also lucky no one really paid her any specific attention either because then they would have seen the daggers she was shooting the ginger tramp.

“We met at a coffee shop,” Nat replied, resting her head on her hand and looking at Rio with big loving eyes. Barf.

“That’s so boring,” Agatha snorted.

Rio tilted her head. “I thought you would swoon over the meet-cute.”

“Meeting in a coffee shop is not a meet-cute.” Agatha said, rolling her eyes.

Rio stuck her tongue in her check. Uh-oh. “Sorry, we couldn’t pull up to The Getty, Agatha. Not everyone gets a true meet-cute.”

This bitch. “You wouldn’t.” Agatha threatened, waving her knife around menacingly.

“Okay, I will take this away,” Lilia said, grabbing the knife out of Agatha’s hand.

“Oh, it’s a butter knife, stop exaggerating,” Agatha rolled her eyes again.

“Is this from the iconic first meeting?” Alice prodded, and Agatha wondered how many times she could roll her eyes before they fell out.

“Mhm,” Rio smirked.

“Wait, what is happening?” Nat perked up.

“They had a crazy first meeting,” Jen filled Nat in, leaning over conspiratorially.

“But they won’t tell anyone about it,” Alice whined.

“All we know is that it was hilarious and that it happened at The Getty,” Lilia provided helpfully.

“We just found out it happened at The Getty,” Jen deadpanned.

“Come on, babe. Tell us!” Nat nudged Rio with her shoulder.

“Well, I always try but someone here might actually shoot me.” Rio said, rubbing her hand sweetly on Nat’s shoulder.

Agatha ran her finger across her throat with a lot of menace.

“And that’s that.” Rio said, moving the subject swiftly to something else. Agatha didn’t know whether to be relieved or annoyed.

“I’m going to go to the little girl’s room.” Agatha said abruptly and not because she dropped her fork, looked under the table and watched Rio and the whore play footsie.

She stood quickly, chair jutting out, ready to make her exit when Nat perked up, “I have to go too!”

Agatha spun around, wide-eyed. “What?”

But Nat was already getting up and fixing her dress. Agatha felt like a cornered dog. She tried to get away faster, like they weren’t going to the same place, but suddenly she was tripping headfirst into a waiter and being doused with an obscene amount of water. Who fucking carries that amount of water in a single tray anyway? Was the waiter running for a fucking world record?

“Shit, Agatha, are you okay?” Rio jumped up and ran over to Agatha who was soaking wet on the floor next to a million glasses.

“What do you think, buddy?” Agatha sneered, still taking Rio’s hand and letting her haul her up anyway.

“I think I have a shirt in my trunk!” Alice bolted out the door. No waiters hit her on her way out. Fucking assholes, this was fixed!

Agatha stomped to the bathroom, Nat and Rio trailing behind apprehensively.

“Are you okay, Agatha?” Nat asked hesitantly.

“I fucking got an entire swimming pool’s worth of water poured on me, of course, I’m not okay,” Agatha barked. Nat seemed to shrink under her gaze. But it only made Rio comfort her more.

Agatha slammed the door of the bathroom far too violently.

“Agatha, you need to chill.” Rio tried, but Agatha locked herself in a stall and leaned her forehead on the metal door.

“I need a minute,” she whispered, hoping Rio would understand and leave her alone.

“Okay.” Rio said from the other side. She heard someone wash their hands and then the door closing.

At that moment, for no specific reason, Agatha felt like crying. It definitely wasn’t because of the water that had been spilled all over her and the fact that she was sure the makeup had melted off her face and how her dinner was most definitely ruined. It might have been because of the way Rio was fucking looking at Nat all night. The way it was clearly so much more than sex. The way it was un-fucking-fair.

What did the ginger bitch have that Agatha didn’t? Agatha was hotter. Objectively. She was more successful. They were literally at her promotion dinner. Oh, and most importantly, she knew Rio so much fucking better than Nat ever better, better than even Rio knew herself. She was there when Rio couldn’t crack her thesis film, sitting out in the cold, half a pack of cigarettes smoked, questioning the state of the world. She was there when Rio didn’t want to go home for the summer, sleeping on Agatha’s couch, working at the local burger joint. She had seen her at her worst. She had been there at her best. She knew how Rio thought, what fueled her, why she ran, why she cried.

It should fucking count for something right? Like a call or a warning, like hey, I’m bringing a redhead nightmare to dinner, you good with it? Something.

That’s what was eating Agatha inside. The inconsideration.

She deserved a text from her best friend letting her know that she asked someone else to be her girlfriend. That she had swapped around her entire worldview. That she had miraculously cured all her attachment issues. Because it was courteous. Because Agatha would have had time to process all the emotions she had trapped shut at the bottom of the tartarus sized pit in her heart. The feelings she barely whispered to herself.

You know, the ones that burned through her when she and Rio lay side-by-side, not touching, but breathing the same air and she felt safe and whole. Or when she called Rio at seven in the morning and Rio, half-asleep, dodged morning rush traffic to come sit with her while she cried. It was the comfort they had built for years. It was the scraps Agatha accepted so hungrily because she knew that Rio and her would never be right. There would always be ultimatums and walk-outs and toxic make-ups. That they would drive each other off a cliff. That Rio would never date.

And now she was having to swallow a very painful pill. That Rio never wanted to date her.

Because the truth was right there, staring at her with such painful force. They never touched. Ever. No casual brushes, no hugging, no hanging off each other. Rio was basically human jelly, she leaned against everything and everyone without worry, but never Agatha. Not like Agatha sought her out anyway. They were always close, side by side, never touching. No casual friendship touches. No touches at all.

They never did the emotional stuff either. The affirmations and words of encouragement. There was a whole six months Agatha thought Rio hated her because she wouldn’t talk to her about something that was not work or her thesis. But she talked to Alice. And Lilia. And even fucking Jen. Talked to them and touched them and leaned on them. But Agatha brushed it off as a quirk of how close they were, that they didn’t need to hold each other's hands. That they knew who they were to each other and were secure in just knowing each other completely.

But the nail in the coffin, the most damning thing that came back to her in that moment and nestled in her heart, was Rio forgetting Agatha’s screening and not realizing until a whole four days later. Four days that Agatha cried and almost murdered everyone during. It didn’t matter that Rio was home during that time, dealing with her parents. It didn’t matter Rio didn’t really give an apology. She fucking forgot. Agatha had swallowed many excuses of her own making then.

But Agatha knew her place now. All the lies she told herself melted away and she felt the full brunt of her delusion, clear and simple. She knew where she belonged in Rio’s life, and it was not near the top.

“Agatha, you okay?” Alice asked from the other side of the door.

“Yeah, fine,” came Agatha’s watery reply.

“I have a shirt for you!” Alice threw a large white shirt above the bathroom stall. Agatha caught it and threw it over her damp dress.

“Thanks,” she said when she walked out, hoping Alice would ignore her red-rimmed eyes and the splotches all over her face.

But Alice wasn’t the only one out there, was she?

“Agatha, are you okay?” Rio looked at her, worry creasing her face.

“Never better,” Agatha tried to say cheerfully but it came out a lot more robotic than she hoped.

“Agatha,” Rio stopped her and tried to reach out, but pulled away before she made contact. “Did I mess up? Should I have not brought Nat?”

Yes. Get her the fuck out of here. “No, no, it’s all okay. Just been a long day,” Agatha lied through her teeth.

She was dying inside.

“Okay, good. I really like her. I want her to hang out with us more.”

She was never going to recover from this.

Agatha flashed her best attempt at smiled and turned away, washing her face in the bathroom sink and hoping a snake would crawl out of the tap and kill her. No such luck. Pity.

Alice had already returned to the table and when Agatha and Rio came back into the restaurant, everyone turned to her with sympathy.

“If one of you says you’re sorry or even utters a word about how you feel bad, I’ll leave here screaming, change my name and move to Mexico.”

Rio burst out laughing beside her. “I would pay good money to see you in Mexico.”

“¡Espero que mueras en el infierno!” Agatha said in broken Spanish, but it only made Rio laugh harder.

Agatha huffed as she sat down, rattling the silverware.

“This reminds me of the day we met,” Rio said as she dried her eyes.

“Oh, please, come on, it’s been years, just tell us!” Alice groaned.

Rio looked over at Agatha and raised her brow. Agatha felt a rush of happiness that she violently suppressed. Fuck it. Rio wasn’t hers. So why should she keep this story wrapped away then?

“Tell them,” Agatha mumbled. Rio’s eyebrows shot up her forehead. Everyone cheered.

“Seriously?” Rio leaned forward, trying to make sure she heard Agatha right.

Agatha nodded. “You can tell them.”

Rio looked very shaken, but quickly recovered, a brilliant smile taking over her face. “Uh, um, okay, so let me set the scene.” She cleared her throat dramatically, and Agatha was already regretting this. “First thing I do as a freshman is I join this ‘Women in Film’ group chat, right. I thought it would be super fun but it’s these girls just going at it, like immediately, what is your Letterboxed? Who's your favorite filmmaker? And I am freaking out because everyone has this crazy niche taste and I am from fucking Delaware so I get super intimidated and don’t really say anything. And I watch this one girl, boy, she’s going crazy, like blowing up the chat talking about a BBC television show from the nineties about Pride and Prejudice.”

“It wasn’t about Pride and Prejudice. It was Pride and Prejudice. Uncultured swine.” Agatha snarked.

“Let me guess, you were the girl?” Lilia smirked.

“She was,” Rio replied, smiling bigger. “And she really sold me on this show, even though it was like seven hours of very period-accurate television. And the next day she went off in this ninety people group chat about a different weird TV show and I was like, who is this girl? Keep in mind, we were freshmen.”

“We were literally film majors, Rio. Having an opinion on film is our entire education. It literally comes with the territory.”

Rio rolled her eyes, but there was no frustration, only fondness. “Anyway, a few days later, I saw this exhibit was going up at The Getty about life in the eighteen hundreds and for some reason I kept thinking about the girl from the group chat and I didn’t want to go alone, so I asked her to come with me.”

“And she said yes, and I bought the tickets. And the whole morning I was shaking, like fully shaking. My freshmen-year roommates were like where are you going and when I told them, they convinced me it was a date, like I had asked her out on a date, and I was like no, it can’t be, and I started to hyperventilate.”

Of course, it turns out to be Agatha. And she gives me so much shit for it the entire way to The Getty.”

“And we go to the museum, and we are talking, normal topics, but the entire time I can’t figure out if it was a date or not.”

This part tracks. Agatha couldn’t figure out if it was a date either. But she thought that was more what happens when two clearly queer women go out.

“But it’s going great, we talk for like three hours straight and then we go to a farmer’s market and go get food. And suddenly, she was like, I have to go home. And I am like, what? But she flags down a cab and we get in, food in one hand, water in the other and we are still talking and suddenly, she throws up all over the back of the taxi.”

“That’s it, we are cutting you off,” Lilia said, flagging down a waiter who shot her a very dirty look as he took away the broken glass.

“Did you not hear Rio recount the most embarrassing thing that has ever happened to me?” Agatha whined.

“That was the second glass you personally broke, Agatha,” Jen said from her other side. “Not to mention the thirty you accidentally broke earlier.”

Agatha muttered something along the lines of a death threat but didn’t order another drink, instead folding her hands tightly.

“She walked me to the dorm, I puked my guts out for a week, and we have been friends since.” Agatha finished, ready for this to be done.

“Yes, much more interesting than a coffee shop.” Agatha said, malice intended.

“Agatha, I can’t believe you threw--” Before Jen could finish her thought, Agatha picked up her steak knife and stabbed it really close to her hand.

“Never mention it again,” Agatha said simply.

“You non-stop sociopath!” Jen yelled.

“Need a ride?” Rio said, leaning on the wall next to her.

“Nah, she drove here and wanted to drive back.”

“Oh.” Agatha looked up at Rio. Her hair looked like it had been pushed back again and again. Agatha wondered what it would feel like to run her hands through that hair.

“Sure,” she choked out, when all she wanted to say was sure, take me home to my sad studio apartment where I will spend the night dreaming of you.

Rio smiled and took her keys off the carabiner that hung from one of her front belt loops. Her car was not far at all, but Agatha felt like it was an eternity. She wanted to memorize every movement, how Rio’s hair swayed at the ends when she walked, how she had folded her formal blazer up to her elbows, which would seem annoying and stupid on most people but it revealed her toned forearms and Agatha was surprised how that could make her weak in the knees.

She hated how Rio would smile at her and she would melt. She hated how she wanted to be here, in this moment, forever. She hated how Rio didn’t love her. She hated that she cared.

Rio opened the door for her, without asking. Agatha wanted to cry.

Rio played her favorite music, popping open her favorite playlist without even hesitating. Agatha needed her to fucking stop.

“Oh, I didn’t say it,” Rio said as Agatha put on her seatbelt. “Congratulations on your promotion to editor! You finally did it!”

Agatha smiled. “Thank you.”

“Can’t believe you let me tell them the story,” Rio smirked.

Agatha shrugged. “It was time.”

“Didn’t think you would ever say that,” Rio said, tapping her fingers on the wheel as they waited for the light to turn red. Agatha lived close by, thankfully.

“People change.” Agatha offered. Because that is all she could give. Only three more streets.

“Yeah, people do. Thank god, we never dated,” Rio said casually.

Agatha almost died.

“What do you mean?” She whispered.

“I mean, I was so close to asking you out that day. But I am glad we are friends. We would have killed each other if we got together. Here we are,” Rio said as they pulled up to Agatha’s apartment building.

Agatha felt her heart breaking. It felt like it was suddenly a sieve and everything, all the pain and longing and sadness of the years that Agatha had hoped and wished and prayed for Rio, just burst through. She tried laughing but it came out closer to a mangled sob. She tore the seatbelt off, and climbed out. Just before she closed the door, she leaned in, possibly making the worst mistake of her life.

But she didn’t care. She had to say something.

“Rio,” she said softly. Rio looked up, smiling fading once she noticed Agatha’s expression.

“I would have loved to be yours.”

Chapter Notes

so didn't expect that response... thank u for all the comments (even the screaming)! im so glad you guys liked it and i am sorry that the ending wasn't as happy as we wanted it to be so i wrote more!!

this was going to be a two-shot but it has now turned into a four-shot. i will earn the happy ending tag i swear!! but first, we suffer.

Rio Vidal was losing her mind.

She was sitting in her car in the driveway of Agatha’s apartment building and she couldn’t move.

I would have loved to be yours.

What the fuck? What the fuck did she mean? Because if she meant that she would love to be Rio’s then Rio would have to invest in an early grave.

I would have loved to be yours.

The image of Agatha being hers was too overwhelming. Too, too much. Even though Rio secretly dreamed of it every goddamn night. Even though Rio whispered it like a prayer when she thought no one was watching. Because it couldn’t be true. Agatha never looked at her like that.

She doesn’t even know how she ended up at Lilia’s. She was trying to go home.

“Rio?” Lilia had opened her door, already in her night clothes, looking like she was ready to go to bed. “What the hell are you doing here?” She stood in the doorway, arms crossed.

“What--What does it mean?” Rio said, walking by her and into the house.

“And you’re coming in,” Lilia shook her head. Rio was already taking her shoes off.

“She said she would have loved to be mine.” Rio was now pacing.

“Who did?” Lilia fell back on her couch. “Nat?”

“No, Agatha. Agatha told me she would have loved to be mine.”

“Oh shit.”

“What does that mean?”

“Rio, I think we both know what it means.”

“No, does-- does it mean she loves me like a friend? What does ‘be mine’ mean anyway? She isn’t a thing to own. Or does she-- or--”

“Rio.” Lilia grabbed her by the shoulders and shook her. “Why do you care?”

Rio wasn’t listening. Rio was pulling her hair out. Rio was pacing.

“Why did she say that? What did it mean?”

“Oh boy, I am going to need backup for this one won’t I?” Lilia stalked out, muttering under her breath as she roused the neighbors. Alice and Jen very conveniently lived across the hall.

Rio couldn’t hear her. Rio couldn’t breathe. Rio was hyperventilating.

Did Agatha love her? No. She said loved. Which means past tense. Which meant Rio missed her chance. Rio somehow missed her chance with Agatha. That should have been impossible. There was never a chance in the first place, right? They spent so much goddamn time together, surely Rio would have caught that Agatha wanted there to be a chance. What the fuck.

Why did she say it like that? I would have loved to be yours. Like she couldn’t just be? I would have loved to be yours. She could be. Rio was going to throw up.

“What did she say? Exactly.” Jen asked when she came in, Alice and Lilia a step behind.

“I would have loved to be yours.” Rio all but yelled.

“Damn, I didn’t think baby girl would ever come close to admitting the big crush she had on you.”

“What?” Rio came to a screeching stop and stared at her three friends. “What did you say?”

“You heard me,” Jen said, throwing her legs on the coffee tables in front of the couch.

“Agatha had a crush on me?” Rio choked out.

“Rio, come on, you have to have seen it.” Lilia said, gesturing wildly to the space around her. “We all saw it for years.”

Rio did not see it. In fact, Rio did not know how it could be obvious considering how much time Rio spent staring at Agatha. Wait, years?

“I--I didn’t know.” Rio whispered.

“Rio, tomorrow we are going to the doctors and getting that autism diagnosis, I swear to god.” Alice muttered behind Rio.

“So, she had feelings for me?”

Everyone nodded slowly. Rio was going to have to spend so much money on her expedited funeral because her heart was going to fail in the next five minutes. She could feel it dying.

“Has or had? Does she still? How long have you guys known?”

“I think you are missing the point here, Rio.” Jen said, crossing her arms. “Don’t you have a girlfriend?”

Rio stared blankly. Agatha hadn’t said yes yet.

“Nat?”

Oh shit.

“Did… did you forget about Nat?” Jen said eyebrows raised.

“No. Yes. It doesn’t matter.”

“Rio, why do you care if Agatha has a crush on you or not?” Alice asked, slightly suspiciously.

Because it-- because--

They were sitting in the film lab, screens blinking in the darkness, people clicking away, losing their minds. Rio and Agatha sat side by side at adjoining monitors, secret snacks between their stations. They weren’t allowed to have them, but that’s what made Agatha bring them in the first place. They were working on their separate theses, and it was not going well. AVID was on a super personal mission to make them cry.

Agatha’s hard drive had almost corrupted twice, but she was able to recover it from the backup on the computer. Rio had seen the doom spiral spin thrice, but lived. Two separate IT support people had to console them when they realized one of the dailies didn’t fully load.

It was one of the most excruciating days of her life.

And then Agatha leaned over and handed her a red box. Rio turned it over to find speciality Kit-Kats, the Sakura Green Tea ones, the ones she had grown up eating, no savoring because she only got them when her best friend brought them home from Japan. The ones she could not find anywhere in this godforsaken country. But they were here, in her hands. Somehow Agatha had found them.

She looked up at Agatha, brow raised, questioning. Agatha just shrugged.

“There’s a store that sells them nearby.”

“No, there isn’t.”

“There is in San Diego.”

“You drove all the way to San Diego to get me these?” Rio choked out.

“It was no biggie.” Agatha turned back to her screen.

“We live in Los Angeles.” Rio stuttered out.

“It was on the way.” Agatha was already pulling her headphones up.

Rio wanted to kiss her. Rio wanted to cry.

Why did it matter?

Because it changes everything.

“Because it changes everything,” Rio said out loud.

Rio remembered when Agatha decided she was going to be a theatrical director and was going to put on a very ambitious student play. She remembered how she offered to stage manage even though she had no fucking idea what she was doing. Anything for Agatha, that was what she lived by then.

Let’s be honest, it is what she still lived by now.

She spent the next three weeks googling what a show bible was and how to notate blocking and what a daily call was and watching youtube videos on how to call a show. She was so in over her head. But then she would go to rehearsal and Agatha would start talking and Rio would lose all sense and reason. Because she was a visionary. Because she brought out feelings in Rio she didn’t know she had. Rio had spent her entire life running and for the first time in existence, all Rio wanted to do was stay and listen.

She remembered wanting Agatha to stay back and talk through the next day’s schedule when they would finish, Agatha would make a joke about them being partners.

And it made Rio come alive.

Because that is what they were. Partners. Doing this together.

Rio knew when Agatha didn’t understand a scene by the fact that she let the actors talk more. Rio knew when Agatha was tired because she always showed up with blue Gatorade. Rio always had sour worms on her table because she knew that Agatha inhaled them when she was stressed.

For those three weeks, they were each other’s lifelines. And it meant everything.

“Because--” Rio started but the words died on her tongue.

Because Agatha meant everything.

Because if Rio thought there was ever a chance she would have torn the world apart.

“Rio, sweetie, you have such a wonderful girlfriend. I think you should move on from whatever this is.”

She never knew she had something to move on from. Nat was smart and sweet and kind but she didn’t know how to talk Rio off a ledge when she was scared and she didn’t have unruly hair that made Rio want to run her hands through it all day long. She didn’t put Rio in her place with one scathing comment. But mostly because she wasn’t Agatha.

Because Rio’s entire existence wasn’t wrapped up in her.

Rio stopped listening then. “I have to go, I have to talk to--”

Lilia interrupted then, shaking her head. “Rio, do you think she’s just jealous?”

Rio froze. “Jealous?”

“I mean, we all know how jealous she can get. Remember when she dated Wanda?”

How could Rio forget?

The Wanda era haunted Rio. Agatha had met Wanda after the brief but enthusiastic attempt as a director. Wanda was a Theatre major, capital T. She lived, breathed, ate her craft as an actor. Rio had thought Wanda was weird when she first met her, but Agatha had found Wanda endearing.

The next thing Rio heard Agatha had invited Wanda for a movie at her place.

Within a week, they were dating.

“You move fast,” Jen had said when she broke the news to their friends.

“Well, when I want something I get it.”

That pierced Rio deeper than she would like to admit. She thought about it longer than she should have, night after night for months, silently crying when she thought Alice had slept.

Why didn’t Agatha want her? It was a hard pill to swallow.

Wanda and Agatha were like a wildfire. Suddenly, Wanda was everywhere. They basically UHauled within the first three months of their relationship. Wanda all but moved into Agatha’s single in the sophomore dorms. Their wardrobes merged. Their personalities merged. They spent all day together. All night. All their friend game nights and movie nights and all of Rio’s late night facetimes with Agatha. Wanda was always there, lurking in the background.

Agatha and Wanda dated for little more than a year. Rio was mostly okay during that time, especially once she successfully suppressed her stupid feelings and befriended Wanda.

Rio, begrudgingly, only with a very big gun pointed to her head, would admit she actually did like Wanda. They were very similar people. They made similar jokes. They liked the same music. They had the same nonchalance when Agatha’s theatrics flared up.

There were times Agatha was cooking and Rio would talk to Wanda. They would joke about how Rio was Agatha’s work wife and Wanda felt like a mistress. They would whisper conspiratory over Agatha’s big moments and Wanda would always ask Rio if Agatha was okay. Because the saving grace through it all was that Agatha still kept Rio closer to her than anyone else.

It always seemed like Wanda tried too hard with Rio, like she was trying to impress her somehow. Rio never understood why Wanda seemed to need her validation so much, but she let Wanda fester for a while before she gave her the friendship she so desperately sought.

And then Agatha broke it off. No reason, really. Just ended it.

Wanda had tried talking to Rio but Rio was as confused as she was.

“I have no idea why, Wanda,” Rio was trying to calm down the sobbing woman who was throwing Agatha’s things into a box.

“Oh, I am sure you know why,” Wanda wailed, throwing a shirt in the box.

“It was out of the blue for all of us, she just went home and we don’t know what happened there, who said what, and now we are here,” Rio tried again.

“Rio, don’t be fucking stupid. You know why, hell, even if I don’t want to admit it, I know why.”

Rio didn’t get any chance to figure out the reason because Agatha called then and Rio went running.

When she got to Agatha’s apartment, Agatha was drunk.

“What are you doing?” Rio had wondered, half surprised, half concerned.

“Pre-gaming.”

“Pre-gaming?”

“Yup, we are going to the theatre club party.”

“We are going to the theatre club party?”

“Is your brain broken? Why do you keep repeating what I am saying?”

“Why are we going to the theatre club party?”

“Because I need to win the breakup, Rio.”

“There is no winning, Agatha. You dumped her. You won. She’s going fucking crazy.”

“Well, I need to bury her then.” Agatha took another swing of the vodka bottle.

“Why did you do it?” Rio was suddenly very brave.

“It’s just vodka.” Agatha tried shrugging it off.

“No, no. Why did you break up with her?”

Agatha was silent for a while. “She wasn’t who I thought she was.”

Before Rio could prod any further, Agatha’s phone started buzzing.

“Taxi is here!” She said cheerfully and Rio knew Agatha was not making it back home herself.

“Fuck, give me a second.” Rio grabbed her keys and wallet and ran behind the mad woman.

They arrived at an abandoned warehouse that had been converted into an off-site theatre venue that student groups used sometimes, and which was far more bustling than Rio thought it could be. Theatre nerds, they knew how to party.

Before Rio was even fully out of the car, Agatha already had two drinks in her hand.

“Oh, thank you,” Rio said, reaching her hand out for the second drink.

“Get your own,” Agatha yanked the drink back and chugged it sloppily, wiping her mouth with her arm and throwing the red solo cup in the bushes.

Okay, Agatha was acting more unhinged than usual. Something was up.

“Agatha, what are we doing here?”

“I told you,” Agatha said, eyes roaming the crowd. “I’m winning.”

“Why does it matter?” Rio tried a different tactic.

“Will you make out with me?” Agatha suddenly turned to her, desperation lacing her voice.

“What?” Rio would have done a spit take if she was drinking anything. Thankfully, she was not. So, she stood there gaping instead.

“Oh, for fucks sake,” Agatha said, turning around and shoving her tongue into the first girl she found.

Rio realized why. Across the room she saw Wanda, crying, staring at the scene in shock.

“She’s jealous, Rio.” Alice emphasized.

Jealous of what? Rio wanted to ask. Jealous of whom?

“Let’s go find her,” Rio said instead. “Ask her these questions, you know, instead of speculating.”

“Right now?” Lilia asked, baffled.

“This actually might be the most sensible way to go about it.” Jen chimed in, looking around for Lilia’s car keys.

Alice was throwing on her jacket. Lilia groaned and walked out behind them. They all piled into her car and she sighed as she walked up to the driver's seat.

“Where to?” Lilia asked but Rio was already putting Agatha’s home address into the GPS.

They got there in record time. Partially because Lilia was an insane driver who should not have a car (and even more so should not have a driver’s license), and partially because Rio was vibrating so hard Lilia was scared she would explode.

And then Rio was knocking on Agatha’s door. Okay, it was more like pounding.

Agatha opened the door. She was wearing barely there pajama shorts and a thin camisole, a black floral robe that hung loosely around her, exposing her shoulder.

“Rio?” She said slowly. “What are you doing here?”

“What did you--” Rio started and then she saw the angry mark on Agatha’s neck.

“Who is it?” came a familiar voice from inside the studio.

Wanda.

Wanda was there. In Agatha’s apartment. In the middle of the night.

“Who is there?” Rio heard Lilia ask. But Rio had stopped processing.

Fuck, Rio felt so stupid.

Why did she think this could be different? Why did she think this could be anything? She was going to give up a sweet, nice future with Nat for this?

She probably said it because she was jealous. It meant nothing.

“I didn’t-- You-- Why are you here?” Agatha trembled.

“It doesn’t matter,” Rio cut in. “We are leaving.”

“Wait--” Agatha reached out, grabbing Rio’s hand. “Please tell me, why are you here?”

Tears filled Rio’s eyes looking at Agatha’s hand holding her wrist.

They never touched. Never.

“I thought I had a chance.” Rio looked up to find Agatha staring back at her with shock. “Turns out, I was wrong.”

Rio shook her hand out of Agatha’s hold and fled down the stairs.

Chapter 3

Chapter Summary

agatha was wrong? hmmm... let's all think again.

Chapter Notes

200 kudos??? omg!! thank u all!!

also, i lied. it's now a six parter? maybe. I haven't finished it yet but i'm having a lot of fun writing the angst (i enjoy torturing myself and apparently you all) and i promise it will be a big pay off!!

i am churning out like a chapter a day so i promise the pay off will not be far if u stick w me!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness was a fucking idiot.

No, way worse than a fucking idiot.

“You’re genuinely the biggest moron I have ever met,” Jen told her in no uncertain terms after Rio ran away.

“She-- she-- why?” Agatha’s brain felt like it was on fire. Words were melting in her skull.

Why was Rio at her door so late at night? What did Rio mean when said she thought she had a chance? She was the one dating someone.

“What the fuck, Agatha?” Alice said, crossing her arms.

“No, what the fuck, Rio!” Agatha said pointing after Rio.

“Why did you say what you did and then go call your ex?” Lilia sniped, raising her brow.

“Are you all forgetting the dinner we were at like what three hours ago where Rio brought her girlfriend?” Agatha said, her brain finally returning from the prolonged trip it was on. “I didn’t do anything wrong! She doesn’t get to do this. She doesn’t get to be the victim. Rio is dating someone else.”

Everyone had the decency to look embarrassed.

“You’re right. We’re all drunk and not thinking correctly. We’ll see you tomorrow,” Lilia said, shuffling the lot away. “Good night, Agatha!”

“And Wanda!” Alice called as they left.

“Was that Alice?” Wanda said once Agatha closed the door and leaned her forehead against it.

“I think you should go,” Agatha said firmly, not looking at Wanda.

Wanda sighed and moved to grab her bag from the couch.

“I saw this coming,” Wanda said as she threw stuff in her bag. “You were always too in love with her.”

“I am not-- was not in--” But Agatha couldn’t finish her sentence. Because all that flashed through her mind was Rio’s face when she realized that Wanda was there.

“She has a girlfriend.” Agatha finally whispered out.

Wanda looked at her with sympathy. “You loved her the entire time we were dating, Agatha. Girlfriend means nothing with the two of you.”

Agatha could feel the tears escaping her eyes. “I’ve ruined it now, haven’t I?”

“Agatha, you could stab her repeatedly and she would still look at you like you are everything.”

Agatha froze. “She looks at me like I am everything?”

“God, you two really are idiots.” Wanda sighed again, looking at Agatha’s tear stained cheeks. “I can’t believe I am offering this, but I can talk to her. Tell her that we didn’t really do anything.”

They didn’t, they truly didn’t. They kissed for like forty-five seconds and then Agatha sobbed in Wanda’s arms for two hours. It wasn’t her fault that she bruised easily.

“I don’t know, Wanda. I don’t know if we will recover from this. I don’t know why I said what I did.” Agatha was trembling now. Wanda stood up and put her arms around her in a platonic show of affection.

“Agatha, do you remember what you did when we had that screenwriting competition and you didn’t think you had a chance because Pepper Potts was entering?”

Agatha nodded. “I said fuck it and I wrote the best thing I have ever written in my life.”

“When you think you have nothing to lose, you always follow your heart. You thought you lost Rio, so you finally, finally did the one thing you have been dying to do since you met her.”

Agatha looked into Wanda’s eyes. “And that is?”

Wanda looked visibly stricken. “Oh my fucking god, I take it all back, there is no hope. You are fucking stupid. You just did the thing, Agatha, you did it! You told Rio how you felt. What do you mean ‘and that is?’ I can’t with you two, I fucking can’t!”

And with that Wanda barged out of Agatha’s apartment, but not before giving Agatha a kiss on her cheek and smack on the back of her head.

Agatha was, as some would say, in a state of denial. She didn’t really cry or yell or process anything that night. She pushed it all down, drank a copious amount of vodka and passed out on her bed.

It was easier that way.

The next morning Agatha woke up with the worst hangover known to mankind. The birds were chirping too loud, the sun was too bright and Agatha did not set any alarms the night before. When she looked at her phone she almost fell out of her bed.

She was so fucking late for Jen’s pre-birthday brunch.

Fuck, fuck, fuck.

Agatha threw a white sundress on, grabbing her strappy wedge heels and cherry red purse and ran out the door, paying no attention to her unkempt hair or puffy face. Her phone died right as the Uber arrived and she almost spilled the entire contents of her bag when they went over a particularly large speed bump, but she made it.

Only forty minutes late.

“I’m sorry, I’m sorry,” Agatha apologized as she found them in the restaurant. Jen crossed her arms when she saw her.

“And what is your excuse?” She demanded. Agatha squirmed under her gaze.

“My phone died?”

Jen rolled her eyes. “Sit down. Can someone get her a mimosa?” Jen looked around for a server.

Agatha sighed in relief and searched for an empty chair. The only one left was opposite Rio.

Fuck.

Agatha took a seat with as much grace and false confidence she could muster. She flashed a smile in Rio’s direction but Rio immediately looked away.

Double fuck.

Monica, who was sitting to her left, turned around and smiled at her. “Long time no see,” she laughed and squeezed Agatha into a warm hug.

“How have you been?” Agatha accepted her warmth. Better than dealing with the frigid cold stare coming from the other side of the table.

“I’m doing great!” Monica beamed. “Just moved into a new house, got promoted at my job and oh, look at the baby we are fostering.”

“You and Darcy are fostering a baby?” Agatha squealed. She fucking loved kids.

“Yes, look,” Monica pulled out her phone and scrolled through an entire folder of baby pictures.

“She’s so small,” Agatha cooed. “Hi, baby.”

“She’s a delight!” Monica smiled, then nudged Agatha. “I thought you would have definitely popped one out by now.”

Agatha grabbed her chest in mock outrage. “I didn’t expect this from you. I am barely thirty.”

Monica rolled her eyes in jest. “Yeah, but you were always so crazy about kids. I always thought being a mom was a part of the plan.”

Agatha sighed. “Just haven’t thought about it for a while, you know. Haven’t found the right person to think about these things with yet.”

She heard a scoff from the other side of the table. Agatha looked up to find Rio’s stare piercing into her.

Monica was laughing though, clearly not picking up on the tension.

“I always thought you two would pop out a few children,” Monica said pointing between her and Rio.

I did too. Agatha thought, but instead she choked out a feeble, “What?”

“Nothing, just that you two would have the most chaotic kids. Like they would get your stubbornness and Rio’s hyper-fixations and they would drive you up the wall.”

Agatha tried so hard to just look at Monica and not at Rio. She couldn’t let Rio see her heart break at those words.

Because Agatha had thought about it. A lot. But how do you tell people that in every vision you have of children, all of them have your best friend’s face? How do you say that you can’t imagine kids without Rio also sitting there digging or climbing trees so you chose not to think about that part of your future at all? You know, the more apt question is, how do you say that without someone making a call to the local psychiatric facility?

There were tears in Agatha’s eyes, she could feel them almost fall, but she coughed and used it as an excuse to wipe them away.

“That’s such a funny thought,” Agatha tried brushing it aside. “So, how’s Darcy? You two seem happy.”

Monica smiled and launched into a long update about the status of her relationship. Agatha snuck a quick look at Rio, thinking she would find her pissed or stressed but instead Rio just looked hollow? Far off, like she was imagining something wonderful.

She couldn’t be imagining the same thing as Agatha, could she? She couldn’t.

Agatha forced her attention back to Monica and soon enough, the brunch was ending and everyone was saying goodbye.

Agatha had confidently walked out with Monica, only to realize that she forgot her purse. When she double-backed, she saw that Rio had already grabbed it and was walking towards her with new determination.

Fuck, this is what reckoning looked like.

Agatha expected Rio to explode. Force her to say something she didn’t want to say. She was ready for Rio’s anger. Hell, she was angry at herself for calling Wanda last night.

But she wasn’t ready for Rio’s apathy.

“Here’s your bag,” Rio said, tossing it at her. “You forgot it.”

Agatha stood there frozen. Rio didn’t even stop, she just walked on past her.

Agatha knew she should say something, ask Rio for a ride, her phone was dead, everyone had left, ask about last night, fuck, ask about Nat, but all she could think about was how easily Rio had thrown her away.

It shouldn’t have mattered that Wanda was over last night. Rio had a girlfriend.

It shouldn’t have mattered if she fucked Wanda for god’s sake. She had a girlfriend. Something Rio promised she would never have. Something Agatha had secretly hoped would only happen with her.

“Rio!” She called out, before she could stop herself. She didn’t need to turn around to see that Rio had stopped. “Can you give me a ride home? We could talk.”

Agatha heard a low laugh. “After the last one, don't blame me if I don’t trust you.”

“Trust me?” Agatha swung around to find Rio, stomping to the entrance where she stood. “Why do you not trust me, Rio?”

“You do stupid shit when you are jealous,” Rio barked back.

“Jealous? Why would I be jealous?” Agatha said with far too much bite.

“I don’t know, maybe because I finally found a stable, wonderful girl to date me and you couldn’t?”

Agatha took a step back. Is that why Rio thought Agatha would be jealous? Maybe they were idiots all along.

“That’s not why-- I didn’t--” Agatha stammered. Then, in one singular moment of clarity. “If you think that’s why I said what I said, then I guess you never knew me at all.”

Something painful flashed across Rio’s face and quickly disappeared. “I guess I never did.”

And Rio walked away. Agatha’s eyes followed her as she hopped into a car.

A car that Natasha was driving.

So, this is what it feels like to have your heart shatter irrevocably, Agatha thought as an unbearable pain gripped her and tore her insides out. This is what it means to lose the only one in your life you thought you didn’t have to live without.

Agatha watched them drive off, no longer keeping it in. No longer even trying to pretend she didn’t love Rio with everything she had.

Chapter 4

Chapter Summary

coming to you with more avoidant lesbians... will they figure it out?

Chapter Notes

im sorry i keep lying. this is now a full fledged fic. will keep writing the avoidant lesbians until they find each other i dont care how many chapters it takes. stay tuned for the elusive happy ending i keep proising (it'll come. it's a matter of when not if!!)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio Vidal was happy.

She was so happy. She had a lovely, stunning, gorgeous girlfriend she should be swooning over. She had a great job and a wonderful group of friends.

So why did it feel like someone had ripped her heart clean out of her chest?

By the time Nat picked her up from Jen’s brunch, Rio had stopped speaking. Nat looked at her with concern, wondering if she needed anything, but Rio’s mind was running at such a pace she didn’t have space to talk. She barely had space to breathe.

If you think that’s why I said what I said, then I guess you never knew me at all.

She was just saying things to fuck with Rio. She was just trying to cover her own ass by trying to make Rio feel like shit. She was trying to make Rio fold.

I guess you never knew me at all.

Why was Agatha so good at getting into Rio’s head?

She hated it. She hated it all.

She hated how she noticed how good Agatha looked in her white sundress, calves exposed, shoulders bare. She hated how she noticed her face was swollen and her arms still had angry red marks from the way she slept. She hated how she liked how Agatha was taller than her in those stupid strappy heels. She hated how excited Agatha got when looking at Monica’s baby pictures. She hated the thought that Agatha would have children with someone else.

It shouldn’t have been as revolutionary as it was. ‘I always thought you two would pop out a few children.’ It should have been just a throwaway comment. People joked about it all the time. About how Agatha and Rio were work wives and basically married. About how they sometimes used to parent juniors in college or their friends when they were drunk. Agatha was Mom, Rio was Dad, and they were always going to give you a piece of their minds. It was a running joke.

It shouldn’t have been as chaos-inducing as it was, but all Rio could imagine was a girl with Agatha’s hair refusing to brush it before school and a boy with Rio’s eyes running around the backyard and Rio coming into the house full of dirt after gardening for hours and Agatha frowning at the mud she tracked into the house but kissing her anyway and she felt like her heart was exploding.

Because she wanted it. She wanted it so desperately. She thought she was strong enough to walk away, but she never realized how much of her existence was wrapped up in Agatha.

Nat didn’t push further, even though she should have. They drove to Rio’s house in silence. No music, no conversation. Just Rio’s manic heartbeat filling the space.

She had walked away from Agatha. She had not even given her a chance to say anything.

Not that it would have mattered, a voice echoed in Rio’s head. She chose Wanda.

She always chose anyone but Rio.

“Rio, are you going to tell me what is going on?” Nat asked.

Rio blinked. They were in her room. She was laying on the bed and Nat was sitting cross-legged next to her. How did they get here?

“I--I can’t-- I don’t” Rio muttered, unable to get the words on her tongue out.

I can’t stop thinking about Agatha. I can’t stop wishing I got the chance to love her. This isn’t fair to you. I can’t stop. How could she say that to Nat? How could she say any of this to Nat?

“Do you want me to call Agatha?” Nat asked, already pulling out her phone.

“No!” Rio yelled.

Nat looked taken aback. “O-kay. I won’t. I just thought it might be nice talking to her. On our first date you said she was your safe place.”

Rio started to cry. Not like a few tears, no, big sobs. If Nat thought she was crazy before, hell, she must think she was insane now.

“Rio, I’m sorry, I’m sorry. I don’t know what I said that was wrong but you don’t have to worry, I won’t call Agatha.”

That just made Rio cry further. She felt like sorrow had gripped her heart and seeped into her bloodstream. She felt it overtake her, engulf her. How was she supposed to move on? She felt like she lost her best friend and the love of her life in one fell swoop. She feels like she lost it all.

Because of whom? Wanda?

Why was it always Wanda?

Why did Agatha never say anything earlier? Why didn’t Rio see it earlier? All those times where she thought those feelings in her were just friendship? Why did she drag Nat into this mess? Why couldn’t she drag her out? Rio felt like her world was closing in. She couldn’t figure out what was reality and what was a memory.

“Rio,” Nat was speaking, but it felt very far off. “Can I ask you something?”

Rio felt herself nod.

“Why did you and Agatha never date?”

Suddenly, Rio’s mind stopped. All the chaos and anxiety and pain just froze and she was consumed by the question.

Why didn’t they ever date?

Rio remembers wanting to ask Agatha out the week after the museum. She remembers checking in on Agatha and her stomach bug and telling her she had a lot of fun at their not-date date. She remembered Agatha not replying with coherent words, just a string of unconnected emojis. She remembers swooning over them and pacing the room as her freshmen roommates offered advice to her on how to ask Agatha out but they were all straight and she was only half-listening, because she felt literal butterflies in her stomach.

And she remembers Agatha calling her that night.

“Rio?”

“Agatha, I was just thinking about you.”

“Oh.” Agatha sounded like she had been crying.

“Are you okay?”

“I just-- I need a friend.”

“I can be there in ten minutes.”

Rio remembers running over to Agatha’s room and finding her outside her door, eyes red, ghosts of tears still running down her face.

“Are you okay?” Rio asked again.

“Can we just walk around?”

They walked around campus in silence. But it wasn’t a bad silence. It was a silence that said thank you, for just being here. It was a silence that felt like coming home after a long day and having a hot plate of your favorite food waiting on the counter and the love of your life singing in the shower.

They finally ended up on some hills by the tennis courts. Laying in the grass. Staring at the stars. Just existing.

“My mother called,” Agatha finally said. “She’s such a raging bitch.”

“So is mine,” Rio responded, leaning back further into the grass.

“Do you ever feel like sometimes you are completely alone in the world?”

Rio looked over. Agatha was staring out at the stars, looking so broken.

“Sometimes, yeah. Sometimes, but I wish I had no parents at all.”

“My mom cut me off today. Said I wasn’t good enough to be her child.”

“Oh fuck, Agatha, I’m so sorry.”

Agatha waved her off. “I’m more worried about who will be my emergency contact now.”

Agatha looked over at Rio then, and realized that in the grand scheme of things they could date and end up hating each other, just like her parents did or they could support each other forever. Maybe they needed to be friends a lot more than they needed to be anything else.

“I can be.”

Agatha looked at her in surprise. “You would do that for me?”

Rio nodded. “You never have to worry about that, Agatha. You never have to worry about being alone in the world. As long as I am here, you will always have a friend in the world.”

“We don’t think of each other like that,” Rio said instead. Nat narrowed her eyes.

“Bullshit. I have no idea what Agatha said to you last night, but you are not okay and I have a very strong feeling it has to do with the fact that you’re in love with her.”

“What?” Rio choked out. “I am not in--”

But Nat just gave Rio a look that said I am not a fucking idiot and Rio folded.

“It doesn’t matter. She’s with someone else.”

“So, were you, and it didn’t change how you felt.”

“I-- It-- wait, were?”

Nat smiled kindly. “Rio, you’re great, you are smart and kind and totally in love with someone else. We will never work out.”

Rio wanted to laugh and she would have if she also didn’t want to cry.

“This is so pathetic. I am so pathetic.”

“No, you are not.” Nat moved closer and cupped Rio’s face in her hands. “You are not pathetic. You both are just scared. But I promise you, love isn’t scary. And you two, the way you know each other, the way you love each other. It will be worth it.”

Rio let out a watery laugh. “This has to be the most lesbian-coded break up in the world. My ex is telling me to go get with my best friend.”

“Well, if the shoe fits,” Nat laughed.

Rio picked up her phone, ready to call Agatha, ready to listen, to say everything, when an incoming call from an unknown number popped up. Rio declined it, pulling up Agatha’s contact when it came through again.

Rio answered, ready to tell the telemarketer off as she heard, “Is this Rio Vidal?”

“Yes,” Rio responded. “I’m not interested in--”

“Ma’am, I am sorry to inform you that Agatha Harkness has been in a serious accident and was taken to Westview Presbyterian today. We have been trying to contact you for the last thirty minutes because you are listed as her emergency contact. We recommend you come here as soon as you can.”

Rio’s heart stopped beating.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 5

Chapter Summary

agatha makes a choice. is it a sensible choice? obv not.

Chapter Notes

300 kudos??? omg this is wild!!

also i am so sorry. just know, it gets better soon.

tw: homophobia, minor child abuse.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness swore she was not blind.

She was just hysterical and her brain was foggy from crying so hard. That’s why she didn’t see the car coming at her.

All she remembers is a shout and looking up just in time to see the car coming at her but not enough to move away and then she remembers Rio’s face.

Her warm brown eyes. Her smile. The way she scrunches up her nose when she is scared.

She remembers every time she wanted to lean over and kiss Rio. She remembers Rio holding her hand during her grandmother’s funeral. She remembers a lifetime of going to sleep on FaceTime and watching stupid nature documentaries about bees and ants and sharks. She remembers reading about poisonous plants and doing witch rituals together on full moons. She remembers hugging her and promising that they would last forever.

And then, she remembers nothing. A black, endless void.

Beep. Beep. Beep.

Agatha felt like someone had stuffed cotton in her head and asked it to be a substitute for her brain. She felt woozy, like everything around her had been doused in syrup and had the integrity of jelly. Everything was moving. Everything was not solid.

“Agatha?” A voice came. It felt very far.

“Rio?” Agatha heard herself say, but she had no idea how she opened her mouth.

“Agatha?” This time it was louder.

It was not Rio. It was Jen.

“She’s waking up, she’s waking up,” Jen said to someone else in the room.

“Hey, sweetie, how are you feeling?” Lilia was beside her. When did she get there?

Agatha opened her mouth to respond but there was an oxygen mask on her face.

“No, don’t say anything, rest, please, rest.” Alice looked like she had been crying. In fact, the three of them looked like they had been crying.

Agatha moved the mask away so she could speak. “Who died?” Agatha said weakly.

Lilia looked stricken. Alice burst into tears again. Jen looked like she was choosing between screaming at and strangling Agatha.

“You almost did, you idiot.” Jen said, but there was no bite, only concern. “How do you feel, truly?”

Agatha felt like she was on a cloud. She really did not feel that bad at all.

“Like I am about to walk out of here tomorrow.” Agatha said confidently, removing the mask and laying it on her chest.

All three of them looked at her with such pity.

“Seriously, I am fine. I promise!” Agatha whined, trying to get up. Lilia held her down.

“Don’t fucking move. You fractured three ribs, broke your leg, almost tore your elbow open and oh, yeah, you have a gigantic hole in your lung.” Lilia threatened. “You’re not leaving any time soon.”

Agatha looked down at her body in the hospital bed. True enough, there was a cast on her leg, bandages everywhere and wires and ginormous cannula in her arm.

Before anyone could utter a word a doctor walked in. He looked like a kind man with geeky rimmed glasses.

“I am Doctor Banner,” he said with a smile. “How are you feeling, Miss Harkness?”

“Surprisingly, fine. Nothing hurts.”

“Is this normal?” Lilia piped up from near her.

“It’s the drugs we gave her,” Dr. Banner said, pulling out a torch and running it by her eyes. Agatha blinked back in surprise. “You had quite the accident, Miss Harkness.”

“Agatha, please.”

“Agatha, you have a long road of recovery ahead of you. We would like to keep you here for a little longer, monitoring your lungs and heart. Just in case.”

Agatha nodded, eyes shifting from the doctor to her friends. “So, I got the good stuff?”

The doctor grimaced. “Yes, you could say you got the good stuff. I have paused the oxygen, but we will ask you to put the mask back on if your oxygen drops again.”

Agatha nodded. He smiled as he left, promising to come check in on her. She could see the worry on her friends faces but she felt surprisingly lucid. She felt no pain at all, actually. So, she decided to do what any rational human does and inflict the pain on herself.

“Where’s Rio?”

All three of them suddenly looked anywhere but at her.

“She’s-- she,” Alice stuttered and then stopped, tears leaking out of her eyes.

“She’s not here, is she?” Agatha said, trying not to cry.

“No, no, she is.” Lilia said and it sounded suspiciously like she was trying to cover something up. Lilia looked through the window in Agatha’s hospital room that overlooked the nurse's station, and waved furiously.

Agatha followed her gaze and saw her. Rio, hair up in a claw clip, eyes screwed in focus, leaning over a clipboard and writing in it.

She was here.

And then she saw Nat leaning over Rio, rubbing her arm. Comforting her.

Rio laughed.

And Agatha felt all the pain she wasn’t feeling a moment ago.

Because she was stupid in thinking that this changed anything at all. Rio still loved someone else. Rio didn’t love her. Even while Agatha lay in this hospital bed, hurt and almost escaping death, Rio wasn’t sitting there next to her. No, she was with her girlfriend. Laughing. Agatha felt her heart shatter again and again.

But then she felt rage. So much pure, unadulterated rage. Because how fucking dare Rio bring Nat here? How dare she rub it in Agatha’s face? How dare she do this again and again?

Agatha couldn’t stop remembering a certain memory. A certain feeling.

Evanora sitting on the edge of Agatha’s bed, staring down at her in disgust as she tried on prom dresses, whispering about all the ways it made Agatha look ugly.

Evanora showing up to parent teacher conferences and asking, “are you sure you are talking about my daughter?” whenever teachers praised her.

Evanora and her long, burgundy nails that dug into the skin of Agatha’s arm whenever she was too much. Too loud, too animated, too friendly. The angry red marks that stayed beneath long sleeved shirts, pierced skin that let Agatha know that she had overstepped, she had to shrink, make herself smaller, make herself less.

Of all the time spent in her room with her father’s old camera, fidgeting, exploring, trying to capture the world through her perspective, hoping that maybe if her mother saw it her way she would breathe, relax, open up a little.

Everything in her house was white and expensive and Agatha still remembered how hard her mother slapped her when she accidentally spilled something on the couch. Because her hearing was less important than inanimate furniture.

She remembers the feeling, alone in her room, too scared to say anything, too scared to breathe, feeling like there was no place for her, needing to run away, needing to claw her way out.

She remembers her mother finding out she was gay. She saw the last bit of care for Agatha die in her eyes. She remembers packing her things that night, knowing she would never come back.

She remembers a lifetime of being too much and not enough. Of wanting someone to love her and them turning their back.

Agatha had felt like a used tossed tissue then, uncared for, unloved, worthless. To be used and forgotten, irrevocably damaged for anyone else.

And here she was again. Feeling the same inability to change her fate. Feeling the same rejection.

Though the way Rio hurt her was nothing like the way her mother did. It wasn’t as bad, but in some ways, it was far worse.

Because Rio was probably going to spend her life kissing Nat and telling her how much she loved her and proposing and having her babies and Agatha was going to die heartbroken and alone.

Rage now seeped into her bones. Because Rio should know better. Because Agatha was stupid enough to think people were good. Or maybe her mother was right. Maybe she was evil. Maybe she deserved nothing.

She remembered the first time she thought she could have though. She remembers it because it is seared into her brain.

The first time they went to a college party. Agatha had gone out of her way to find this little black dress she was sure would torment Rio within an inch of her life. She had taken time to dress up, hell she wore heels. She was ready to make Rio regret never making a move.

“Hey, you got any perfume?” Rio had said when she walked in. Agatha turned around so Rio could see what she was missing and then promptly lost her mind.

She wore a brown strapless dress, so simple, so Rio, and she looked fucking delectable. The dress hugged her just right, tight enough that Agatha could see the curve of her breasts and her nipples poking through, but loose enough that Agatha wanted to rip the dress off with her teeth to see what was below. Her hair was curled at the edges and she had attempted a smoky black eye and a sharp red lipstick that made Agatha’s insides melt into a monster that chanted Rio’s name like it was her religion.

And maybe it was. Because she was so fucking stunning Agatha’s brain went blank.

Agatha stood there gaping, mouth opening and closing, for at least five minutes. Rio had grabbed the perfume from Agatha’s desk that she had converted to a vanity, sprayed it and touched up her mascara.

“You good?” she asked Agatha who had not moved from when Rio had walked in.

“Your dress…” Agatha muttered. And your collarbones. And your neck. I want to bite your neck.

“Is it not pretty?” Rio asked, smoothing it down nervously.

“No! I mean yes, it is very pretty.”

Rio beamed. “Thanks, I was worried it was too simple. I thought I needed a necklace or something, but I didn’t have one.”

“You can take one of mine!” Agatha said too quickly.

“Oh, yeah, didn’t think of that, let me just grab one.” Rio disappeared. Agatha had to remind herself to breathe.

She forgot how beautiful Rio could be. Rio always opted for comfort, dressed in casual jeans or sweatpants. Agatha had never seen her like this, so perfectly crafted. So perfectly crafted for her.

“Ready?” Rio said, coming out of the room with Agatha’s “A” necklace hanging off her neck. Agatha almost had an aneurysm. She was too afraid to say anything, though, worried if she pointed it out Rio would take it off.

Maybe it meant something, Agatha foolishly hoped. Maybe it meant what she wanted it to mean.

It swayed on Rio's neck all night. When she drank out of a red solo cup at the party. When she danced. When she made out with a random girl and went home with her.

That’s when Agatha found out that no matter how much you love someone, they always hurt you.

You know what, fuck this shit.

Agatha didn’t need her. She didn’t need her as a friend, she didn’t need her as anything. Her feelings for Rio were like a fucking parasite, gnawing away at her reason, making her weak and sappy. If Rio didn’t want Agatha then Agatha did not need Rio.

Agatha would never move on, not in the sense that mattered, she knew that. But Rio didn’t need to know. She just needed to know that Agatha was done. Rio could have Nat. Hell, she could have whoever she wanted except Agatha, and that didn’t seem like a problem Rio would care about much at the rate she was going.

And as with most parasites, the only way to get them out is to cut open yourself and rip them from wherever they have burrowed. Harshly. Violently.

“You should rest.” Jen said from beside her.

“Visiting hours are almost over.” Lilia chimed in. “We love you.”

“We will be back first thing tomorrow,” Alice said as they tried to leave.

“Guys,” Agatha said, ripping her eyes away from Rio and Nat. “Could you pass a message from me to Rio?”

They nodded with differing levels of enthusiasm. The door opened slightly, but not significantly, as if someone was coming in. Agatha didn’t care what nurse or doctor overheard her. She steadied herself, taking a deep breath.

“Tell Rio we are done. I don’t want to see her face ever again.”

“What?”

“Agatha, you don’t mean it!”

“You need rest!”

Her friends' protests fell on deaf ears. Agatha was done listening. She was done pining for someone who didn’t love her. This was like Rio forgetting her about the things that were important to her all over again. When Rio just forgot that Agatha existed while all Agatha could think about was Rio. She had promised Agatha she would always be there. And then she broke it, because here she was with her stupid girlfriend not even visiting Agatha who was dying. It consumed her, that everything came back to her, to this one person who didn’t even think to visit her, who didn’t love her.

Agatha was done.

Chapter 6

Chapter Summary

let me introduce you to the real villain of the story

Chapter Notes

I have a super early work day tomorrow so i am posting this rn but this is tomorrow's chapter (just pretend it's tomorrow)!

floored by the responses yall, really keeps me engaged and writing!!!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio Vidal was not okay.

She was nowhere close to being okay.

She made it to the hospital in ten minutes, blatantly ignoring the red lights at traffic stops, almost swerving into oncoming traffic and barely missing running over a girl who was texting and crossing the sidewalk. The last one was not her fault, really.

She sat in the waiting room, heart beating wildly, her whole body on fire. She felt like the world was ending.

Because it was.

Because Agatha was in the hospital. She had been hit by a car. Everything seemed so fucking stupid then, all this back and forth. Like there ever was a chance Rio could love someone else. Like there was ever any doubt that Agatha wasn’t the one.

And now, Agatha was lying in a hospital bed fighting for her life. For both their lives. Because Rio knew she wouldn’t survive losing her.

“Miss Vidal?” A nurse called out from the station.

Rio shot up and ran over. “That’s me, do you have any updates about Agatha?”

“Miss Harkness sustained a fracture on three of her ribs and her left leg, she had a large laceration on her elbow, but we are more worried about the pneumothorax.”

“What is a pneumothorax?”

“Collapsed lung.”

Fuck, fuck, fuck.

“Do you know how she got hit?” Rio was going to fucking murder whoever’s fault this was.

The nurse flipped through the paperwork. “The EMTs said that witnesses said she was crossing the street to her Uber when a speeding car hit her.”

No. Fuck.

“She has been unconscious since she came in, so we will need you to fill out these forms for insurance purposes,” the nurse handed her a stack of paperwork.

“Can it wait? Can I--”

“We can wait to have her fill it out when she wakes up, if you would prefer.” Rio eyed the ginormous stack of papers and sighed.

“No, no. I can do it. She doesn’t need to worry about this. Uh, when can I see her?” Rio asked, voice wavering.

“We are moving her from the emergency room to a semi-private room since we have to formally admit her into the hospital. Once you finish the forms and she has been moved up, you can see her,” the nurse answered kindly and left Rio with the never-ending paperwork.

Rio sat back down in the waiting room, heart beating wildly. She tried focusing on the paperwork, filling in the insurance numbers and providers and everything she could remember, but her vision got blurrier with every minute.

Agatha’s lung had collapsed. She broke three ribs. She was not okay. She’s lying there, all alone, thinking Rio didn’t love her more than life itself.

People around her were talking but suddenly it felt like the world had slowed down.

Agatha got hurt because of her. She didn’t give Agatha a ride. She said she didn’t know Agatha at all. She was so fucking stupid. It was all her fault.

Rio didn’t realize she was crying until the woman next to her offered her a tissue.

“You should answer that,” the woman said when Rio accepted another tissue, pointing to the phone ringing on her lap. She didn’t even hear it ring.

“Where the hell are you?” Jen questioned when she picked up the phone.

“The hospital,” Rio answered, trying and failing not to cry.

“Rio, I don’t have time for your jokes. We have been waiting at the--”

“No, Jen, I am at Westview Presbyterian. Agatha got into an accident.”

“Fuck, is she okay?”

Rio started crying louder.

“We are all on our way,” she heard Jen say, but Rio was hysterically sobbing now.

She couldn’t lose Agatha. She couldn’t. She loved that stupid idiot more than life. Fuck, she was Rio’s life. For ten years Rio had loved her from afar and she couldn’t live with a reality where she wouldn’t get to do it for real.

Fuck, fuck. She fucked it up. She was the reason Agatha was lying there.

Rio made a promise to herself at that moment. If Agatha made it out of this, she was going to do whatever Agatha asked of her.

If she asked Rio to drive her home, Rio would.

If she asked Rio to kiss her, Rio would do so every waking moment.

If she asked Rio to be friends, just friends, Rio would stand by her side forever, watch her fall in love, be her maid of honor, do it all.

She would do anything. As long as Agatha kept breathing, she would do anything.

“Rio! Rio, is Agatha okay?” Lilia was there in front of her.

“Where is she?” Alice was not far behind.

Rio couldn’t really stop crying long enough to tell them anything. Alice wrapped her arms around Rio, trying to soothe her.

“Miss Vidal,” she heard through all the noise her friends were making. Rio bolted to where the nurse was standing.

“Is she here?”

“She is here,” the nurse said, gesturing to Rio and her friends to follow. She led them down a hallway to a semi-private room, a suite with two beds and a plastic curtain dividing them. On one of those beds lay Agatha.

Rio immediately found her side. Tears streaming down her face she grabbed her hand and held it close to her heart. She kissed her hand repeatedly, refusing to let it go.

“Miss Vidal?”

Rio looked up to see the nurse who handed her the forms earlier looking at her with sorry eyes. “There is a problem with the paperwork.”

“What?” Rio choked out.

“There seems to be a problem with the insurance. They rejected Agatha’s hospital stay.”

“I’m sorry, what the fuck?”

“Can you come with me?”

Rio looked over at her friends, finger pointing, threatening. “Don’t move, okay. If she wakes up, don’t tell her about this. I don’t want her to worry. I will figure it out.”

Rio leaned forward and kissed Agatha’s forehead. “I love you,” she whispered softly. So simply. Because it was that easy. “Don’t go anywhere.”

And she ran behind the nurse, following her outside where a woman stood, glasses perched on her nose, clicking on the keyboard of a computer perched on a travelling portable work station.

“Hello, Miss Vidal. My name is Miss Temple and I am a Billing and Insurance Specialist. I am here to help you figure out what is going on.”

Rio nodded as the woman launched into a very long and complicated monologue about Agatha’s insurance deductibles and out-of-service providers and out-of-pocket costs.

“Wait, stop, can you just tell me why they rejected her claim?” Rio said ten minutes in, understanding nothing so far.

“The insurance company said that she doesn’t need to stay in the hospital. It wasn’t an emergency.”

“She has a collapsed lung.”

“The company claims she could have gone home since we are just keeping her here to monitor her and it was non-emergent.”

“Once again, she has a collapsed lung. And broken bones. And is unconscious.”

The woman launched into another spiel about insurance and Rio soon realized that she was not there to help Rio at all, no, she was there to help the hospital.

“I just need to make a call, one second.” Rio said, stepping away and pulling out her phone. She dialed the number, hands shaking.

“Rio?” Nat said when she answered. “What happened, you ran out of here so fast, I couldn’t make out what you were saying.”

“Agatha got into a really serious accident. It’s bad.”

“Oh god, Rio, I’m so sorry. Can I do anything to help?”

“You can, actually. You work for an insurance company, right?”

“In security, but yes.”

“Do you know your way around an insurance policy?”

“Oh my fucking god, the insurance company rejected her hospital visit didn’t they?”

“They did. Almost immediately. Can you help?”

“I am on my way.”

Nat was there barely fifteen minutes later but by the time she did, Rio was drowning in paperwork. They had taken over a section of the nurse’s station because Rio refused to not have a visual of Agatha for this long, so a nurse had raised her blinds and positioned Rio so she could see her from the corner of her eye at all times.

“Okay, what is happening?” Nat asked, reaching over and grabbing a copy of the insurance company’s response.

“I really don’t know, Nat. They rejected her claim and the hospital bill was already going to be a few thousand dollars with the insurance, and I am too scared to look at the number if we have to pay this entire thing out of pocket.” Rio was almost in tears. She circled another thing in the policy that seemed important. “I think you need an advanced degree to figure this out.”

Nat rubbed her arm in an attempt to comfort her. “We will figure this out. If not, we will just let Jen lose in the hospital.”

Rio laughed, relieved to finally get some help.

Suddenly, Rio saw movement in Agatha’s room. Lilia was looking over at her, a pleading look in her eyes, frantically waving for Rio to come in.

“I think something is happening, I am going to go check on her.” Rio said, extracting herself from the papers.

“Go, I got this,” Nat said, taking over the spot Rio was in and turning to the administrator with a burning look in her eyes.

Rio flashed her a grateful smile and rounded the corner, opening the door.

And then she heard it.

“Tell Rio we are done. I don’t want to see her face ever again.”
