Chapter 7

Chapter Summary

agatha does not catch a break. rip agatha.

Chapter Notes

taking a brief interlude from the idiots to give you more feelings about my main opps

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness was wrong.

She did feel the pain. It just wasn’t immediately after she woke up. No, it was two hours later, after everyone had left and she was all alone.

She was raging still, thinking of all the ways she would tell Rio to fuck herself when she inevitably came running back with her tail between her legs. Or all the ways Agatha would push her away from their friends if she didn’t. And specifically the way Agatha would make her regret it all, move on and win.

She was so going to fucking win.

But then pain shot through her body. It started at her leg, the broken one, and suddenly searing, electric pain was rippling through every nerve, every vein in her body. It felt like she was on fire, raw and vengeful, and simultaneously like someone was holding her hands and legs and trying to pull every limb of hers apart. It was piercing. It was overwhelming.

She screamed.

A nurse came running in, but Agatha was not coherent.

“Hurt…pain…it hurts!” she yelled.

The nurse quickly injected something into the bag that was connected to the intravenous drip attached to her arm, trying to soothe her further. The pain crescendoed and then dulled, but only slightly. Not enough. Not nearly enough. Her muscles were cramping, her heart was beating. She was shivering. She was sweating.

“What is happening?” Agatha screamed.

“What is your pain level out of ten, sweetheart?”

“A fucking eleven.” Agatha moaned as another wave of pain hit her.

The nurse tapped away on the machines, and then suddenly it felt like someone turned the volume down slightly because Agatha could still feel the pain but it didn’t consume her.

“Do you feel better now, sweetie?” The nurse asked kindly.

“Better,” Agatha choked out. “Better.”

“I’ve given you something that should help you sleep too,” the nurse said, but Agatha was already slipping away.

“Good morning!” was the next thing Agatha heard. She blinked. She just fell asleep. She genuinely did not know how time moved that fast.

“I’m Nurse Danvers. How are you feeling right now?” The nurse asked, but she was a different nurse, not the one who helped her last night. She had short blonde hair and a very sweet smile.

“Uh, sore,” Agatha said as she woke up.

“I’m sorry, honey, you’re going to feel sore for a little while.” Agatha grimaced. Nurse Danvers busied herself with checking Agatha’s vitals.

“Everything looks great,” she said once she was done marking the chart at the foot of Agatha’s bed.

“Press this button if you need anything,” she finished, placing the call button by Agatha’s hand and patting it kindly.

Agatha nodded and then promptly fell asleep again.

When she woke up, it felt like no time had passed at all. The only window in her room overlooked the hallway, so she couldn’t really figure out what time it was anyway. She tried getting up, but the pain reminded her why that was a bad idea. She used the little buttons on the calling remote to push the bed into a more seated position. The little movement still hurt her. She tried to look for her phone but immediately gave up when she saw how far it was. She could do nothing else. She just had to sit there and face the music.

The music being how Rio still had not visited her.

The music being how she might have truly had lost her.

No. Fuck. She was moving on.

She reached out to the table next to her to try to find the phone when she touched something fluffy. She grabbed it and pulled it close and almost cried.

It was Señor Scratchy.

Señor Scratchy was here. Who brought him?

Probably Alice or Jen or Lilia, she thought. Must be feeling guilty.

But either way, Agatha cried into the soft fur of her comfort stuffed animal, thinking of the time Rio won it for her on one of those carnival games on Santa Monica pier. She buried her face in its neck, breathing in his comforting smell of damp fur, vanilla and hints of Rio’s perfume. Rio always hugged the rabbit when she came over, leaving traces all over him. It’s what secretly made him Agatha’s favourite.

Agatha laughed into his fur. How fucking stupid was she? How did she hug him close to her chest every night, inhaling his fur that carried Rio’s scent and wonder why she always dreamed of Rio?

No, no, she was moving on. She was never going to see Rio again.

Why did it gut her just thinking about that?

When Alice and Jen visited later, barely an hour later, Agatha immediately mumbled out, “Did you tell Rio what I said last night?”

“We--I--Um, Jen?” Alice looked over at Jen imploringly.

“She, uh, she knows.” Jen said, staring at the floor. “That’s what you wanted, right?”

No. Yes. What did she want? Not this.

“Yeah,” Agatha said, instead because she only knew how to eat her words in the safety of her own mind.

They sat there for a while, trying to distract Agatha, trying to reminisce and failing because all the fun memories they shared included Rio and they didn’t know how to talk about her so they just didn’t. Agatha didn’t ask where Lilia was, she kind of knew the answer. After forty minutes of Alice and Jen awkwardly stumbling through conversation, Agatha feigned sleep.

“Good night,” they said as they left. Agatha immediately started crying.

She successfully cried herself to sleep. She had no idea why. (She knew exactly why.)

“I love you,” Rio said to her in her dream. She leaned in and kissed her temple. It felt so real she could almost feel it on her skin.

Agatha woke up in tears.

Fuck, she was so stupid. Why did she say it? Why did she say she never wants to see Rio’s face again. Why did she let her jealousy and rage cloud her senses?

She curled her fists and punched the bed. Something heavy bounced. She felt around and found it to be a book, the very sappy romance kind that she secretly loved. Agatha scoffed. This was useless without her glasses.

Her glasses were right next to the water on the side table.

What the fuck?

Who was bringing her things?

Her head said that it was probably Lilia or Jen or Alice. Her heart really wanted it to be Rio.

Nope. Stupid heart. Fuck Rio. She still had not visited.

She spent the day reading the book, grateful for the distraction. She yelled when the main characters were separated because of a miscommunication. Nurse Danvers kept checking in on the progress of the book as she came in to check Agatha’s vitals. Agatha enjoyed telling her what was happening along with her very apt commentary about how stupid the miscommunication trope was.

She hated the miscommunication trope, it was just so fucking stupid. Like if a few words could separate true love, the maybe your love wasn’t fucking true. She still cried when the love interests got back together, still swooned at the big dramatic love confession. Still tried and failed to not think about Rio through it all.

Lilia visited that day, nodding along when Agatha told her about the book, eyes crinkling when Agatha smiled for the first time since she had been there.

She fell asleep more content that night, but she dreamed of Rio again.

“You are the love of my life,” Rio told her in her dream. “Don’t ever doubt that.” Rio was crying and Agatha could feel her tears fall on her neck. The next morning when she woke up, her neck was surprisingly sticky.

“A little birdie told me you love this movie,” Nurse Danvers said when she came in to check in on Agatha in the morning. She waved a DVD of The Parent Trap. Agatha nodded enthusiastically.

She looked at some scans and vitals. “Lucky for you, your head looks better. I’ll put on the movie.”

Agatha squealed. She smiled as she watched the movie, hugging Señor Scratchy close and, for a moment, it felt like everything was going to be okay.

And then the pain returned. Suddenly, quickly, the pain was back. It overtook her. Agatha screamed and pressed the call button twice, four times maybe. Nothing happened. She screamed again, pain engulfing her.

A nurse she had never seen before came running in.

“It hurts,” Agatha cried.

“What hurts?” The nurse asked.

“Everything.”

It felt like her body was on fire, electric impulses shooting through her, stinging, burning her insides. She felt like she was burning alive from the sheer amount of pain.

“Help,” she choked out. “Help, please.” The nurse was tapping away on the machine next to her.

Her insides felt like they would burst through her, ripping her skin and boiling her blood. “More, please.” Agatha begged.

“I have given you all the pain medication I can, Agatha. I am so sorry.” The nurse replied, apologetically.

“Please, I need more. This is not enough.”

Her ribs burned as she talked. Her elbow throbbed. She could feel her heartbeat in her throat. Suddenly, a darkness took over her brain, seeping in through the edges, engulfing her vision, drowning her mind.

It felt like she was drowning in fire. She couldn’t speak, she couldn’t move.

She could hear yelling though.

“What is happening to her?” It was a familiar voice, so familiar.

“I’m sorry, she is maxed out on pain medication,” someone else said. The nurse! The nurse said.

“Why did she pass out from pain then?” the first voice got angrier.

The nurse said something Agatha could not understand.

“You had her on fentanyl this entire time?” the first voice screeched. Why was it so familiar?

“She came into the Emergency Room! It is commonly used for trauma patients! ”

“So, you’re telling me not only is she now going to feel more pain, she will also be in withdrawal for fucking fentanyl?” The first voice was so pissed off. It reminded her of the time Rio almost punched a man for looking at Agatha wrong. Wait, Rio?

Another wave of pain rippled through Agatha’s body. She could feel every bone, every cell in her body and it was all vibrating.

But all Agatha could focus on was that Rio was here. Rio was here.

Agatha felt herself lose consciousness with Rio’s name on the tip of her tongue.

Chapter 8

Chapter Summary

rio traumatizes some nurses.

Chapter Notes

somehow i hit 400 kudos and like 5k hits and like 100+ comments so here is a bonus chapter

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio Vidal was a flaming, hot wreck.

Because what would you be if the love of your life told you she never wanted to see your face again?

Rio froze at the door when she heard it.

Tell Rio we are done. I don’t want to see her face ever again.

Rio was sure that was the sound a death’s knell made.

She hoped she heard it wrong. She could hear Alice, Lilia and Jen defend her. She could hear their pleas, but Agatha said nothing. Rio knew what that meant. It was final.

So, Rio did what she does best. She ran. Suddenly, Rio was outside the hospital, fresh air whipping against her face. She needed to breathe. She couldn't breathe.

She never got a moment of respite, though, because suddenly all three were there, by her side.

“Rio!” She heard Alice yell.

Rio felt suffocated. Rio felt loved. She turned around to find her friends staring at her. Agatha’s rejection had witnesses. It made it all worse.

“She just woke up,” Jen came to her, slinging her arm around her side.

“Rio, she is half unconscious. She doesn’t know what she is saying.” Alice tried to console her.

“You should go see her.” Lilia said out of breath, catching up to them last. “She’s on a lot of drugs, she didn’t know what she said.”

Rio shook her head.

“I can’t. I promised myself I will give Agatha anything she wants.” Rio said, voice raw. “I have to give her this.”

“You are so stupid, Rio. This doesn’t count. She is so hopped up on drugs she couldn’t tell a giraffe from a zebra.” Jen squeezed her waist in a kind attempt to shake her.

Rio shook her head, “She seems surprisingly lucid, Jen.”

Rio turned to move away.

“So, that’s it? You’re giving up?” Lilia questioned, arms crossed.

Rio let out a low laugh and slowly shook her head like the whole idea was ridiculous.

Lilia patted Rio on the back. “Okay, good. Come on, let’s go home. We can come back in the morning.”

“No,” Rio shook Lilia off. “No. I am not leaving. I will stay here.”

“Overnight? Rio, come on, that doesn’t help anyone.”

“Do you really think I can walk away from her?” Rio looked up and eyed all three of her friends who all had different levels of pity and confusion plastered on their faces.

“I love her,” Rio said, voice breaking. “If she doesn’t want to see my face, fine, she won’t, but I am not leaving her. I promised her she will never be alone.”

Lilia shook her head. “You two…”

Rio turned and marched back to the waiting room where she held vigil for the next three days. She only left once to gather some things from Agatha’s house and another time because Jen yelled at her to shower (even then she did it in a record time of twenty minutes).

She was right there when Agatha screamed the first time. She was the one who found the nurse and sent her in blind panic.

Every night, Nurse Danvers would take pity on her and let her sit by Agatha’s bedside, hold her hand and whisper everything Rio wanted Agatha to know.

“I love you,” she would chant. “I love you, I love you. You are the love of my life. Never doubt that.” She would cry into her hair and kiss her forehead.

Every morning, she would hound the doctors for updates. When she found out Agatha was off the oxygen machine, she brought Señor Scratchy so she could hug him freely. When she found out that Agatha was okay enough to do some light reading, she went and brought a paperback she knew Agatha would love. When she heard that Agatha could use screens for a few hours, she broke into Agatha’s house and got her DVD copy of The Parent Trap so she could watch her comfort movie.

Nurse Danvers would always stop by where Rio sat in the waiting room, never questioning why Rio didn’t go in when Agatha was awake, always letting Rio know how Agatha was progressing. By the third day, the nurses were well aware of Rio’s constant presence and invited her to their break room to have her meals. Rio accepted their kindness gratefully, taking the distraction away from the pain of not being able to see Agatha’s face.

Well, that was technically a lie. She saw Agatha’s face every night when she secretly visited her as Agatha slept and every dawn when Rio finally got a few hours of sleep and dreamt of her. She cursed herself every waking breath for not telling her sooner, not even blaming Agatha once for not wanting to see her, accepting her punishment willingly.

Because Rio was a fool. A goddamn idiot for not admitting this sooner. Because she let Agatha go on for ten years not knowing how obscenely loved she was and she wasn’t going to let her go on another minute not feeling it.

It didn’t matter that Agatha didn’t want to see her. It mattered that she was alive. And Rio was going to count her blessings every goddamn day.

So, it was all okay, and then Agatha screamed again.

But it wasn’t a normal scream, no. It was gut-wrenching. It nearly shattered Rio.

“Nurse, nurse.” Rio flagged down the first nurse she saw. “You have to help her. Agatha, she’s in pain.”

Agatha screamed in pain again. The nurse ran in, and Rio contemplated staying out but when she heard Agatha begging and she ran in.

“Help,” she choked out. “Help, please.”

“I have given you all the pain medication I can, Agatha. I am so sorry.” The nurse responded.

“Please, I need more. This is not enough.” Agatha begged. Rio’s heart ripped itself apart.

“What is happening to her?” Rio yelled.

“I’m sorry, she is maxed out on pain medication,” The nurse replied, looking at Rio apologetically.

“Why did she pass out from pain then?”

“We switched her pain medication from fentanyl to codeine.”

“You had her on fentanyl this entire time?” Rio screeched.

“She came into the Emergency Room! It is commonly used for trauma patients! ”

“Did you not clock that even the smallest dose can cause her to go through withdrawal? What the fuck? So, you’re telling me not only is she now going to feel everything, she will also be in withdrawal for fucking fentanyl?”

The nurse cowered. “There is not much more I can do.” She said, running out the door, hopefully to get more help.

Agatha looked like she had passed out from the pain. Rio grabbed Agatha’s hand and pressed soft kisses to it.

“Please be okay,” she prayed. “I won’t survive losing you.”

She gave Agatha one last kiss and ran over to raise holy hell on the hospital staff. She was so not going to get invited to the break room after this performance.

Very luckily for her and very unluckily for Dr Banner, she found him almost immediately after exiting the room.

“You,” she pointed a menacing finger at him. He was right to cower in fear at the look in her eyes. “Why the hell was Agatha put on fentanyl for that long?”

“She had severe trauma injuries,” Dr Banner replied, starting what was probably going to be a very long spiel containing a lot of words Rio did not know.

Rio immediately ripped into him, “Did you not think she would go into withdrawal?”

“It was a risk, but with emergency patients it is commonly--”

“How bad is it going to be?” Rio all but yelled.

“She might have flu-like symptoms and vomit a lot. It shouldn’t be too--”

Rio was seeing red. “Okay, Dr Banner. Here is what you are going to do. This is a teaching hospital, right?”

Dr Banner nodded slowly.

“Good. You are going to get your most trusted intern to sit with Agatha and nurse her through this withdrawal.” Dr Banner opened his mouth and Rio immediately cut him off. “No, there is no room for you to tell me you can’t do this. You will do this. The love of my goddamn life is going to go through hell for twenty-four hours, she is going to be fucking taken care of the entire time.”

“Miss Vidal, we can’t just allocate hospital resources like this--”

“I know this is not your fault, Dr Banner. I know it’s the system and everything, but the woman I love is in pain and I can’t stop it but I can make sure that she makes it out as best she can. So please, help me. I will raise holy fucking hell if anything bad happens to her, so help me god,” Rio said, voice breaking.

The doctor's eyes softened, even in the face of Rio’s threats. “I will do what I can.”

“Thank you,” Rio nodded as the doctor briskly walked off.

“That was quite a performance,” Rio recognized the voice before she saw her. Wanda.

Rio looked up, nodding at Wanda but saying nothing.

“How is she?” Wanda asked, looking at Rio with too much pity for her liking.

“In a lot of pain. She has a hard night ahead.”

It was Wanda’s turn to nod. “Fucking broken system.”

Rio scoffed in agreement. “You have no idea, Wanda.”

“The woman I love?” Wanda said, no tease in her voice. “Did you two…” Wanda trailed off.

“I know you two are something,” Rio said, tears coming back into her eyes as she remembered Agatha wasn’t hers. “But please, let me have this. Let me take care of her.”

“Oh, boy,” Wanda sighed. “You two haven’t talked.”

Rio’s head snapped up. “What do you mean?”

Wanda just shook her head. “I am only saying this because Agatha is fully dying right now and you need to hear it but it should have totally come from her, but nothing happened.”

Rio looked up, brows furrowed in confusion.

“That night,” Wanda continued. “When you showed up at her door in the middle of the night. We did nothing. She literally kissed me for two seconds and then spent three hours crying about how you don’t love her.”

“She-- what?” Rio spluttered.

“You mean so much to her, Rio,” Wanda said, squeezing Rio’s shoulder.

Rio shook her head frantically. “No, I don’t.”

“Yes, you do.” Wanda rolled her eyes. ”You’re just being a dumb lesbian.”

“I am not.” Rio’s lip quivered, “She said she never wanted to see my face again.”

Wanda took a step back. “When was this?”

“Three days ago.” Rio looked down. She refused to cry in front of Wanda.

“What?” Wanda fumed. Rio would have appreciated the attempt at solidarity if she hadn’t been wanting to blip Wanda out of existence for the last few days.

“She doesn’t love me, Wanda.” Rio said, shoulders shaking with the intensity of the feeling burning in her heart. Before Wanda could say anything, they were interrupted.

“Are you Miss Vidal?” A young man in a white coat asked her.

“Yes,” Rio replied, wiping her tears. “Are you the person who is going to stay with Agatha?”

“Yeah, I am William Kaplan.” The boy said, nodding. “I am well prepped about her history and I will be spending essentially the next twelve hours with her.”

Rio grabbed his shoulder before he could move away. “William, this woman is everything to me. Please, please take good care of her.”

“Do not worry, Miss Vidal. I know she must be special. The whole hospital is talking about how you haven’t left the waiting room since she was admitted. You must really love her.”

“She’s the love of my life, kid. Don’t let anything happen to her.”

William flashed her a somber smile and entered Agatha’s room.

Rio turned around to find Wanda with big, large tears streaking down her face. “You haven’t left the hospital since she got admitted?”

“Well, besides to get things from Agatha’s apartment or the one time Jen forced me to shower, nope.”

“Even though you think she doesn’t love you?” Wanda choked out.

“Whether she loves me or not doesn’t matter, Wanda. I love her. I can’t pretend she isn’t everything to me anymore. Not after almost losing her.” Rio felt the tears coming back. “If she tells me to fuck off after she wakes up, I will. I will do whatever she wants me to because all I want is for the woman I love to be happy.”

Wanda looked both sorrowful and murderous at the same time.

Chapter End Notes

all i am saying is this is not going to be an easy love confession fix i am sorry, but good news is longer fic?

on the bright side, progress!!

Chapter 9

Chapter Summary

agatha wakes up. but does she *wake* up?

Chapter Notes

wanted to make this chapter a bit lighter. the angst was killing me too.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness felt like Death personified.

She woke up shivering, but her hair was wet with sweat. She felt like she had been wrung out, like a dirty rag that had been squeezed and pulled until it was half its size. Her broken leg burned and she could feel where her bone split in two because it was throbbing uncontrollably.

A wave of nausea hit her. She tried to find something to throw up in, but all she could really do was lean forward and hope she didn’t heave all over herself.

Someone put a bucket near her and caught it all, rubbing her back in circles to soothe her.

When Agatha was done, she was offered a cloth to wipe her face. She looked up to find a young man with kind eyes.

“I’m William,” he offered.

“Thank you,” Agatha said weakly. “What is happening to me?”

“You are experiencing some effects of withdrawal,” William said softly. “I am happy to say we are mostly done with the hard part.”

“Mostly?” Agatha choked out.

“The physical effects are wearing off. You somehow slept through it which is rare but not unheard of, but you are going to feel a lot more pain for a little bit.”

“Why?” Agatha wondered.

“You’re switching medicines, essentially. It’s like dining at a Michelin star restaurant and then going to a local restaurant. Sure, the food is going to be good at the local place, but your body will keep wanting the better food.”

“Oh,” Agatha said, kind of understanding what he was saying, but her head was pounding relentlessly. It felt like someone had taken a long, serrated knife and was stabbing the back of her head consistently. “My head…”

“Are you having a headache?” William asked, scribbling something on a clipboard.

“It feels like my head is going to explode.”

William leaned over her head and injected something into her intravenous drip. “This should give you some comfort.”

Agatha did not feel comfort for another fifteen minutes. William sat there the entire time, monitoring her, giving her water and helping her get up.

“Don’t you have rounds or something?” She finally asked William after half an hour of him just sitting there.

“Not today,” William flashed a small smile.

“Why not?” Agatha leaned forward, feeling the medication kick in and provide some relief.

“I am under strict instruction to not leave you until the withdrawal symptoms have passed,” William said seriously.

“By whom?” Agatha asked.

“Someone terrifying.” William smiled bigger. “Though she isn’t that intimidating when she’s hiding.”

Agatha swore she heard a sharp cough from behind the curtain on the left side of the room.

“What?”

“Nothing, ignore me.”

“Who is there?” Agatha asked, very confused, craning her neck to look around the empty room.

“Would you like to eat something?” William asked instead.

Agatha narrowed her eyes at his attempt to change the conversation. “What aren’t you telling me?”

“We can get some food from outside. It isn’t hospital regulations but I can make an exception. What would you like? A burger? Pizza?”

William’s phone buzzed then. He looked down and then looked up. “Would you like a greek salad?”

Agatha relaxed a little, nodding. A greek salad sounded great actually.

“Is that the one with the tomatoes and mozzarella?” William wondered. Agatha looked aghast.

“You don’t know what’s in a greek salad? Honey.”

“I’ll find someone to get one for you.” William typed something on his phone, smirked and then looked up. “You should rest while you wait, preferably with your eyes closed.”

Agatha raised her brow. He shrugged.

She leaned back, closing her eyes but ready to snap them open at a moment’s notice. She heard something move, and opened her eyes just in time to make out a figure hurriedly exiting through the door and William trying very hard to not laugh.

“Who was that?”

“A ghost,” William said, a giggle escaping his lips.

Agatha couldn’t understand what was so funny.

Ten minutes later, someone knocked on the door and handed William a bag containing Agatha’s greek salad. She settled into her bed as William put on Lady and the Tramp, another one of Agatha’s favorite movies.

Wait, how did this kid know?

“How did you know I like this movie?”

“A little birdie told me.” William said nonchalantly, but his smirk was back.

The second the opening sequence started, Agatha let go of the lingering questions in her head as to what the hell was going on and just enjoyed the first time in a few days she wasn’t dying from pain.

But her mind didn’t let her rest further. Because after the pain and anger faded away, all she felt was stupid.

Because how the fuck was she supposed to move on from this?

How the fuck was she supposed to live knowing that Rio existed in the world and was with someone else? How was she supposed to live with the fact she ruined the most important relationship in her life because she couldn’t keep her mouth shut? How did she push Rio away so far that she wasn’t even there when she woke up?

She could always apologize and tell Rio she was wrong and grovel and they would go back to being friends. That was the only way they were going to make it out of this and still be in each other’s life.

She could do that. No, she couldn’t.

Minutes later, Alice and Lilia came in, and William paused the movie.

“Who is this?” Alice asked, looking him up and down, noting his white coat.

“I am--” William began, only to be cut off.

“This is my pet. Say hi, pet.” Agatha said, eyebrows raised to see if he would take it.

“Hello,” William nodded seriously.

Agatha narrowed her eyes further. What the fuck was up with this kid? Was he being threatened within an inch of his life?

“Hello,” Lilia said, confusion clear across her face.

“We just wanted to check on you,” Alice said, coming to sit by her head. “How are you feeling?”

“Like I got hit by a car,” Agatha said, finger tapping her chin. “Oh wait, I did.”

Lilia shook her head, endearingly. “You’re sounding like yourself more.”

Agatha smiled. “I feel better, thanks to William here.”

William smiled back. “I’m going to leave you with your friends for a little, be back soon.” He left the room, closing the door slowly.

“Can I ask you something?” Agatha said after the door shut. Alice and Lilia nodded. “Is Rio dead in a ditch?”

They both looked at her like two deer caught in headlights.

“What do you mean?” Lilia said, regaining her voice first. “You said you didn’t want to see her, right?”

“Has that changed?” Alice chimed in, hopeful.

“Not really,” Agatha said, leaning back a little. Then, casually she added. “Just wanted to know where she was.”

Alice and Lilia shared a look.

“Um-- She--”

Agatha raised her brow. “What is everyone not telling me?”

“Your insurance got rejected and she has been trying to fix it!” Alice blurted out. Lilia smacked her arm.

“It was killing me Lilia, I can’t keep secrets, you know that.”

“What?” Agatha said, taken aback.

“Your health insurance company rejected your stay in the hospital, so Rio and Nat have been fighting them relentlessly.” Lilia said somberly.

“Nat?”

“Nat works in insurance, she helped get your claim fast-tracked or something. I have no idea what they are doing but there has been so much paperwork.”

“Oh.” Agatha said, suddenly feeling small. “So, Rio has been trying to help me?”

They nodded.

“Oh,” Agatha said again.

This was how Rio showed her love. Agatha realized. This was always how she showed her love.

She was there when Agatha’s mother disowned her, sitting under the stars, making sure Agatha knew she was not alone.

She was there when Agatha’s dad died, holding her hand throughout the funeral, never making Agatha feel bad for not crying, pushing back against her mother’s taunts, helping clean up as Agatha sat, processing.

When Agatha got a B on her senior thesis, Rio tore the faculty a new one.

When Agatha wanted to stage a play, Rio dropped everything to come help her.

She was there through every bad grade, late night realization, and every doubt she ever had.

Agatha wasn’t surprised Rio was fighting the insurance company, this is just what she did. This is how she showed her love, by solving all the problems for the people around her so they wouldn’t have to worry about them.

“Can you send her in?” Agatha said, surprising even herself. “I want to thank her.”

“Didn’t you say you didn’t want to see her?” Alice said, leaning forward slightly.

Yes, she did. Yes, she was still unbelievably heartbroken and mad at Rio, especially since she didn’t visit her even once. But all the dreams she had been having made her miss her best friend and she just wanted someone in her corner that wasn’t looking at her like she was frail or would break like glass.

She needed to talk to Rio because she was the only one that always told her when she was wrong and stupid and helped her get back on her feet.

God, she just missed Rio. She wished she could just talk to her again without it being such a big deal. You know, without all the baggage and the Nat situation and the feelings.

She just wanted her best friend back.

“Just-- Can you tell her I am calling a pause on this fight or whatever this is? I just want to talk to her.”

They both nodded in understanding, synchronized in their approval and running out the door.

Agatha wondered if she did the right thing as Rio opened the door and walking in apprehensively, worried look on her face.

The second she looked up, and Agatha saw the tears in her eyes, she realized she made the right choice.

It wasn’t Rio’s fault that she was not in love with Agatha.

It wasn’t her duty to pacify and sit by her bedside and kiss her hand. She was doing what she could as a friend. It should have been enough

“Why didn’t you visit me?” Agatha said, crossing her arms unseriously.

Rio looked up, brows furrowed. “You said you never wanted to see my face again.”

“So, you should have sat here with your back towards me,” Agatha said like it was the most obvious thing in the world.

Rio broke into a big beautiful smile. “Why didn’t I think of that?” A small laugh escaped her lips and she relaxed for the first time since she entered.

“Because you’re stupid.” Agatha gestured to the stool by the side of her bed and Rio quickly sat down.

“How are you feeling?” Rio asked, looking deeply into Agatha’s eyes. Agatha shrunk under the weight of Rio’s gaze.

“Like I got hit by a car,” Agatha tried to lighten the mood with the same joke again.

It did not work. Instead, the mood shifted into something serious. Rio reached forward and grabbed her hand like it was her lifeline. “You really scared me.”

Agatha didn’t say anything, she just stared at their hands intertwined, heart stinging from the weight of everything she wanted but couldn’t have.

“I heard the insurance company is acting insane.” Agatha said eventually.

Rio sighed, gripping her hand further. “I am figuring it out.”

Agatha looked up then, noticing the bags under Rio’s eyes and the dried tears on her cheeks. “Thank you, Rio,” Agatha said, squeezing her hand.

Rio shook her head. “Anything for you, Agatha.” She said voice breaking. “You say the word and I will make it happen.”

Agatha let out a watery laugh. “So, how many insurance agents did you personally drive to tears?”

“None,” Rio said, nonchalantly. “Nat is taking care of that part.”

Right. Nat.

Agatha let go of Rio’s hand like it had burned her, trying to ignore how her heart was clenching. “Tell her I said thank you.”

“I will,” Rio said, now looking down. “Agatha, Nat and I--”

“When can I go home?” Agatha cut in, not wanting to talk about Rio and Nat.

“Do you want to go home?” Rio said softly.

“Desperately. I am tired of the hospital. Get me out.”

“I will see how soon we can get you discharged.” Rio said, looking at where their hands were intertwined just a moment ago. She took a deep breath. Agatha knew that look on her face, the quiet determination as she fought through something she was scared to say. Oh, no. No. Rio was going to tell her something bad, something like how she couldn’t see her anymore or she didn’t love her. Something she would never recover from.

“I need to tell you something. Agatha, I--”

“Don’t.”

“Agatha, please, I--”

“Please don’t.”

Rio’s eyes searched Agatha’s face. Agatha’s lip quivered.

“I think I know what you are going to say," Agatha said, tears finding her again. “And I just can’t do that right now, Rio. Can we just go back to being Rio and Agatha, best friends forever? I’m sorry I messed it up, but I just-- I need my best friend back.”

Rio looked down again, shoulders shaking slightly. When she looked up, she had new determination in her eyes. “Whatever you need, Agatha. Whatever you want.”

Agatha let out a small smile. The thing I want from you I can’t have.

Rio slowly got up, “Let me go find the doctor to see if we can get you discharged.”

Agatha grabbed her wrist, holding her in place. “Rio, was it you who got me all the stuff?”

Rio nodded, a small smile curling on her lips. “Had to keep you entertained somehow so you didn’t rip the nurses to shreds.”

She squeezed Agatha’s hand before letting it go, door slamming slowly behind her. There were tears in Agatha’s eyes. She didn’t even try to wipe them away.

But they were friends again, best friends. She could live with this.

Because now she would at least still have a part of Rio, instead of nothing.

Chapter End Notes

they're friends again!!

and we are back to where we started... or are we? next chapters are gonna be less angst but still a lot of idiocy, stay tuned!

Chapter 10

Chapter Summary

rio has an idea. is it a good one? i think so.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio Vidal was pushing a mattress up the stairs.

She would like you to know it was a very heavy mattress, even though it was a twin XL. Looks can be very deceiving. She cursed that neither she nor any of her friends had an air mattress, having instead to use the spare mattress from Lilia’s small guest room instead.

Agatha had gotten the all clear to be discharged from the hospital earlier that day. The hole in her lung had healed fully and she had strict instructions to be back in a week to get her stitches removed from her elbow, she was not allowed to walk without crutches and had to take all her medicines on time.

Rio had run around like a madman making sure that she had everything in order from picking up Agatha’s medicines from the pharmacy, which if she might say was unbelievably and unnaturally complicated, to making sure her fridge was stocked with enough healthy food that she would get through the next month, to now hauling a mattress into her studio so she could sleep there at night and not worry about hurting Agatha.

Because they were friends again.

Because she allowed Rio back into her life. After everything Rio did to hurt her.

And Rio was going to make sure she didn’t regret it.

Even though it broke her heart that Agatha stopped Rio from telling her how much she loved her. Even though Rio knew, for her, there was no going back to just being friends. Even though Rio knew she would spend her entire life being irrevocably in love with this girl.

Because she could see her face again. She could be around her. She could touch her and hug her and love her as a friend.

And it would be enough.

Rio finally shoved the mattress through the door, hauling it to lean against the wall as she moved Agatha’s couch to be parallel with the kitchen counter, clearing space for the mattress on the foot of Agatha’s bed. She ran down to her car after setting the mattress, carrying up the bag of sheets and a comforter that she had kept from her college days, just in case she ever needed it, and a bag of her stuff so she could stay comfortably over the next week at the minimum.

After she was done, she drove quickly to the hospital so she could be there before Agatha woke up. She really was surprised she didn’t get pulled over even once. She honestly should have.

She was really becoming an unhinged presence on the street.

When she arrived Agatha was sitting in the bed, legs hanging over the edge, folding a shirt over the bandage on her elbow. When Rio walked in she flashed her a great big smile and Rio felt her insides melting.

How the fuck had she gone so long not knowing she loved this girl?

Idiot. Idiot she was.

“Ready?” Rio said instead of I love you.

“Just need to find crutches.” Agatha gestured to where her sweatpants were cut off over the cast on her leg. “Doctor’s orders.”

“Did they not give you crutches?” Rio asked.

“There was a two day waiting list to get crutches from this hospital.” Agatha winced. “Might be better off just renting it.”

Rio nodded, rolling her eyes. “More fucking nightmare fuel.” She helped Agatha up from the bed, allowing her to lean against her as she limped out to the waiting room and let her slip into one of the chairs as Rio cleared the final discharge paperwork at the nurse’s station.

“So, finally going home?” Nurse Danvers asked as Rio signed the final forms.

Rio smiled as she signed the final forms and handed it back. “Thank you for all your help. Truly.”

“Of course,” the nurse waved her off. “It is wonderful to see the love you have for her.”

Rio smiled sadly and turned to walk away when she remembered. “Can you thank William for me too?”

“I won’t have to, you can do so yourself,” the nurse gestured behind Rio to where Agatha and William were laughing.

Something happened to Rio’s heart that very much resembled swooning. Over a laugh. She was so pathetic.

“I see you are back to rounds,” Rio said as she walked towards them, a folder of instructions and discharge papers in hand.

“Mhm, as fun as it was to spend time with you, Agatha, I do enjoy my training.”

Agatha smiled. “You mean babysitting,” she teased.
Then, “Why were you babysitting me anyway?”

Rio felt her face pale.

“Uh-- I did-- because--” Billy stuttered, clearly remembering her threats.

“William,” Rio had said, entering the room five minutes after Wanda left. “How is she?”

William’s face was twisted in worry. “She is asleep, which is a small miracle. But her vitals are all over the place.”

Rio sat down next to William, smiling sadly at Agatha. She took Agatha’s hand and held it over her heart. “Mi amor, we will get through this.”

Agatha trembled in her sleep.

“Can I ask you a question?” William said, sitting on the other side of Agatha. Rio nodded.

“Why didn’t you go home? Why did you stay?”

“I am worried something will happen when I am gone.”

“Why haven’t you been sitting with her then? You stay out during visiting hours.”

“She wants to be done with me, she said she never wants to see my face again. Honestly, I don’t blame her. I have been acting like a dick lately.”

“Why?”

Rio shook her head. “Why are you asking so many questions? What is wrong with you?”

When William simply kept staring at her, she caved. “Because I thought I could love someone else. I didn’t realize that my heart was already hers.”

“Why won’t you just-- just tell her you love her? I am sure she loves you too.”

Rio left out a mangled laugh. “See that’s the thing, kid. Just because I love her doesn’t mean she loves me back. I-- I thought for a second she did, but I was wrong.”

“What if I tell her?”

“I’ll report you to the board and then burn your house down.”

William laughed. Rio narrowed her eyes further. “Don’t think I’m fucking around. I will get you fired if you utter a word of this or the fact she was on fentanyl or the fact that her insurance was denied.”

William raised his hands in mock fear. Rio turned her attention back to Agatha.

“I don’t think you're lying so I will shut up now. Wait, no, final question,” Rio rolled her eyes but didn’t say anything to dissuade him. “What happens if she wakes up and she never wants to see you again?”

Rio was silent for a while.

“Do you know what it feels like to breathe after you have been in a tight space for a long time? Like if you are in a small closet or tiny elevator and you think you're breathing fine and the second you step out your lungs inhale the air so fully that you realize that you had been holding your breath all along?”

William looked confused but didn’t stop her. “Agatha and I have been friends for ten years. I know her better than I know myself. I know what makes her laugh and I know when she has been crying, I melt when I see her happy and I want to tear the world apart when someone hurts her. But I never thought it was love. I always thought it was just a state of existence, like blinking or eating. Until now. Until I almost lost her and I realized I had been in that tiny closet all along, not breathing, too scared to walk out and suddenly there was air in my lungs. She is the air I breathe. So, to answer your question, I will walk away but never stop loving her, never be too far. Because I’m selfish and I only know how to breathe when I am near her. Because I only know love in terms of her.”

William was crying when she looked up.

“So, what, you’re going to stay away forever? You’re going to not tell her how much she means to you?”

Rio shook her head. “I’m going to show her, William. I’m going to show her how much I love her every goddamn day. Whether she lets me stay or not.”

William kept muttering, opening his mouth and closing it like his brain was on fire.

“Because I am crazy,” Rio had said eventually, because it was true and also to just stop William’s muttering.

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Where to?”

“The crutches store and then home,” Rio said as she helped Agatha into a wheelchair that a nurse brought over so Agatha could get to the car. William looked at them weirdly.

“Bye Agatha, bye Rio.” He waved, then he added. “I hope you two find a way to breathe together.”

Rio wanted to murder him and squeeze him. The abomination.

“What did he say?” Agatha asked when they got into Rio's car.

“I have no idea, what a weird kid,” Rio said, a small smile curling on her lips.

They successfully rented crutches from a small family owned store just two blocks away and reached Agatha’s apartment building by noon, but the second Rio pressed the elevator button, the little LED sign that showed the floor number blinked and flashed a ‘service not available’ message. She pressed it four more times but the elevator did not come.

It was just fucking working. Fucking hell.

Rio huffed and told Agatha to lean all her weight on her good leg and she moved Agatha’s crutches to rest against the wall. Agatha didn’t even have time to ask a question before Rio had hauled her into her arms and was carrying her, bridal style, up the stairs.

“Fucking elevator maintenance has really gone down lately,” Rio huffed. “What if you were alone here? How would you have gotten up the stairs? You should sue your landlord.”

“Rio,” Agatha mumbled.

Rio kept her eyes trained ahead, very focused on not dropping her. “What? He should get sued. He has not done a single fucking thing since you moved in. Useless man, remember when he got you to pay for a new fridge? And you did-- I still can’t believe you did that. Let’s see how long it takes for them to finish fixing this. If it's longer than a day, I swear I will sue him myself.”

Rio finally looked at her once they had reached the front door. Agatha was red and breathless, like she was the one who had climbed the stairs.

“You good?” Rio asked, tilting her head to her side, trying to read Agatha’s face.

Agatha refused to meet her eyes. “You can put me down now.”

Rio grinned and lowered a little and then pulled her towards her chest like she was curling weights at the gym. “I don’t know, this feels like a great exercise.”

Agatha flushed further. “Put me down, Rio.”

Rio slowly lowered her so Agatha could hop off and gently allowed her to unlock the door. Agatha stepped in, still leaning on Rio for support and immediately froze.

“What happened to my apartment?” she exclaimed.

Oh, yeah. Rio forgot to warn her. “Shit, sorry, I forgot to tell you. I think I should stay here to help you. You still aren’t a hundred percent and I don’t want you to get hurt again trying to go to the bathroom yourself or eating your own cooked food.”

She gestured to the mattress. “Moved this in this morning so you wouldn’t have to worry about sharing the bed.”

Agatha was staring at the room in horror. Her flushed face was paling and a sinking feeling gripped Rio.

“Did-- do you not want me here?”

Agatha was quiet for a while and then shook her head. “It makes sense for you to stay,” she mumbled.

Rio excused herself and brought Agatha’s crutches up the stairs, taking them two at a time, heart beating wildly.

Did she fuck up again? Did she overstep?

And then she walked into the apartment and Agatha had stomped her way to the bed and was sitting bundled up in blankets looking very much like an angry bean burrito, and she realized that she had an uphill battle ahead.

Because the one thing she knew about Agatha, almost like a preacher knew the bible, was that she never accepted help straight up. She always had to be tricked into it.

Rio sighed. This was going to be a long week.

Chapter 11

Chapter Summary

idiots shall idiot.

Chapter Notes

omg 500 kudos??? over 7k hits?? what is happening yall

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness was about to commit murder.

Specifically she was about to kill one Rio Vidal.

Why, you may ask?

Because her fridge was full for the first time in years, full of vegetables and meat and the cheese she liked from the grocery store forty minutes away she never found time to go to but thought about constantly. She was having not one, not two, but three home-cooked meals every day. Even though Rio put too much spice in the food and Agatha grumbled and moaned and ate all of it anyway.

Because Rio went out and bought bracelets with different protection stones, black tourmaline, obsidian, citrine, and forced Agatha to wear it. Even though Agatha didn’t know how the stones would protect her from getting hit by a car again, she did it so Rio could feel better knowing Agatha was safe.

Because Rio kept force feeding Agatha oranges and broth and applied funny smelling salves to her head hoping it would ease her pain. Because Rio would do things like be there to help her get up before she could even call out for her or wrap a plastic trash bag around Agatha’s cast so it wouldn’t get wet when she showered without Agatha even asking.

But mostly because Agatha couldn’t help but want more.

It consumed her how much she wanted this, forever. A future with Rio. How much she loved that Rio’s toothbrush was right next to hers in her bathroom. How much she loved that Rio’s shark pajamas (that Agatha had made fun of relentlessly) were actually made from pictures of sharks Rio had adopted online and tracked all around the world. How much Rio made her feel loved and worthy, just silently supporting her like a partner would, never asking for more, never asking her for anything.

It was making Agatha feel insane. Because they were not together. But Rio had been-- what is the word-- overprotective lately.

Agatha slept for thirteen hours straight when she came back from the hospital and was only woken up by Rio in a blind panic who was convinced she was ‘over-sleeping’ because she had spent four hours doom researching how patients recovered post-trauma and found out that sleeping excessively after a car accident ‘might indicate serious conditions like traumatic brain injuries, psychological stress, or physical injuries’. Agatha looked at her like she was bat-shit insane, told her to shut up and went back to sleep for another three hours.

In those three hours, Rio had printed out four different health plans that Agatha was going to follow, re-organized her entire apartment and cleaned it and taken her trash out and started to do laundry. When Agatha woke up and saw Rio wearing her bright pink ‘Kiss the Chef’ apron, she almost fell apart.

Because it was starting to feel dangerously like Rio was hers. And she couldn’t get used to the feeling. Because she had someone else.

But then Rio had started fixing things, like she lived there too. When Agatha was awake, she could hear a muffled drill or hammer or some kind of power tool that was just fighting the old charm of her crumbling apartment which was honestly held together with duct tape and prayers. She truly paid too much for this dump. Rio fixed the broken door handle, drilled her shelf into the wall because she was paranoid about it falling over in an earthquake, and fixed all the leaky faucets in the house.

She would have made a great superintendent actually. Or husband. Or father.

Nope. Agatha chanted to herself, yet again. Not yours. Not yours.

But then Rio would put down her tools when she noticed Agatha grab her head in pain and come sit next to her and they would talk about anything and everything. Rio would get easily excited, eyes burning with passion as she went off about some obscure fact about sharks or plants and Agatha would forget to breathe.

It all came back to this, to loving Rio. It all felt so domestic, like coming home to the love of your life. Because it was, in many ways. Loving Rio was as tied to her soul as breathing was to her body. No one even came close enough for comparison.

Agatha was so fucking screwed.

Because Rio didn’t stop at the cleaning or fixing, no, she would go ahead and do something so pure and vulnerable Agatha would feel sick. Like drawing a picture of a very pretty plant on her cast, refusing to tell her its name and when Agatha finally figured it out by using Google image and reverse searching it she almost fucking fell out of her chair.

Fucking bitch drew a bleeding heart. Agatha almost bought a knife and killed Rio right then and there. Because this plant Rio had so casually drawn signified a deep and passionate, sorrowful love that went beyond life and death. That is what Rio drew on her fucking cast.

Rio probably drew it because she liked the way it looked or because she meant it as a friend.

But Agatha had clearly lost her marbles because she was too happy to walk around with the woman she loved (who had a girlfriend!)’s drawing of a plant that signified eternal love for the next month. Why did she not rip the cast off her leg and bash Rio over the head with it? She had to stop.

Did Rio know what she was doing to her?

Did Rio know she was irrevocably ruining Agatha forever?

She could feel it, she really was on the verge of snapping and becoming the next Ted Bundy.

Or snapping and shoving Rio against the nearest wall and fucking her into oblivion.

She couldn’t stop thinking about how Rio had so casually picked her up a few days ago and carried up the stairs. How strong she was. How much she wanted to jump her and fuck her until her eyes rolled over and she couldn’t speak, couldn’t move, couldn’t think of anyone else. About how she could see a sliver of Rio’s toned abs when she stood and stretched in the morning and it drove her feral. She wanted to mark every inch of Rio’s skin, she wanted to carve her name into her heart.

Agatha wasn’t going to survive much longer. (She never wanted this to end.)

She needed to fucking talk to someone about this. Someone who were not her friends and were not trapped between Agatha and Rio and forced to choose a side. She needed an objective viewpoint on a platform her friends would never check.

She opened Reddit.

As Rio manically cleaned the house, Agatha wrote out a heartfelt post about what was going on, hoping internet strangers would solve her problems. They did not. They may have made it worse. Get out of the house, they said. It’ll give you some space.

Agatha suggested they go to the park, get some air and Rio agreed. Now, they have a bunny.

A poor abandoned bunny. Because those stupid, cute red eyes coupled with Rio’s big, brown, puppy ones meant Agatha did not stand a fucking chance.

It meant they spent a few hundred dollars on a visit to the vet.

It meant they bought a cage and a pen for the bunny to play in.

It meant their apartment smelled like pee and shit and Agatha loved every moment of it.

Because Señor Scratchy, Sr. (not to be confused with the plushy, who was also Señor Scratchy, now with the added Jr.) filled her heart with a little more joy. And watching Rio and the rabbit interact was taking years off her life.

She would make such a wonderful mother. Snap out of it! Not. Yours.

Even though Rio begged her to adopt the rabbit, you know with her love for animals and plants and nature, yada yada, Señor Scratchy, Sr. liked Agatha way more. It wasn’t even a competition. Agatha won by a million miles. He snuggled into her side any moment he got, and she played with his soft fur constantly. Agatha was suspicious that Rio was jealous of the rabbit.

She ignored what that thought did to her heart.

For the first few days, Agatha did nothing related to the rabbit. Partially because even though Rio would grumble in the morning about feeding the bunny, she would do it before Agatha woke up, and partially because Agatha was very much enjoying watching Rio chase the rabbit around the apartment like a headless chicken.

Agatha would catch Rio trying to bribe the bunny with homemade treats so it would like her, or trying to rub her scent on tissue paper and shoving it in his cage. But the second she let him go, he would come running to Agatha and burrow his face in her chest and Agatha would try and fail not to laugh.

After another day of the bunny straight up rejecting Rio’s love, she tried convincing Agatha to give it to a shelter.

“The apartment is too small for the bunny!” Rio whined. “We should give him to a home where he can jump around.”

Agatha looked down at the rabbit who snuggled closer to her. “Don’t attack my baby. He’s going nowhere.”

“The bane of my fucking existence,” Rio muttered under her breath. “I swear he is smirking at me.” She walked away still muttering.

“I fear your mother has lost the plot.” She said, ignoring the part where she acknowledged that she and Rio were this bunny’s parents and instead focusing on the part where Rio seemed to be beefing with a rabbit.

And then Señor Scratchy, Sr. shat all over Rio’s mattress while she was out running errands. Agatha didn’t notice until it was over, the smell reaching her suddenly and she limped over to throw open the windows just as Rio came in and saw what happened.

“You little--” Rio leaped after the rabbit but he burrowed himself in Agatha’s arms and she just looked at Rio through her eyelashes and Rio folded.

“Fucking roadkill,” she heard Rio mutter as she stripped the sheets and took them out in a trash bag. “When Agatha isn’t looking, I will gut you and cook you in a stew.”

Señor Scratchy, Sr. looked alarmed. Well, as alarmed as a rabbit could look. Agatha tried not to laugh.

Rio came back for the mattress that she rinsed and left outside in the apartment’s shared backyard to dry. Agatha put Señor Scratchy, Sr. back in the cage then, in his little punishment hole because she realized he had just made her life a lot harder.

Because Rio would not fit on the couch. And that meant one thing.

“Are you sure you are okay with me sharing the bed?” Rio asked for the hundredth time, just staring at the empty left side, refusing to get in.

“Rio just get into the bed, I don’t bite.” Agatha finally snapped. Rio immediately got under the covers.

She rolled over, back facing Agatha. Agatha stared at her sleep shirt loosely falling to reveal a slender shoulder and tried very hard to steady her breaths. She turned over too, so they were now back to back. This is not how she imagined the first time they shared a bed would be, backs against each other, not touching, not looking into each other’s eyes, but this was all she had.

And she would take this forever, even if she knew it would slowly kill her.

Chapter 13

Chapter Summary

and we return to regularly scheduled angst

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio Vidal woke up with something tickling her face.

Something soft. At first, she thought it was Señor Scratchy, the plushy, then she thought that the stupid bunny has fucking escaped and sat on her head, but when she blinked open and looked at what was on her face, she noticed it was brown.

It was Agatha’s hair.

Because she was sprawled all over Rio. And Rio’s arms were around her, holding Agatha to her chest, her chin resting on top of Agatha’s head.

She was not brave enough to breathe, no, not when this meant everything. For this very brief moment, Agatha was hers. Only hers. She was in her arms and Rio could pretend for a little that she wasn’t going to run away when she woke up. She still couldn’t believe that she went so long not knowing she loved Agatha, that she spent so long right next to her and didn’t realize that Agatha held the key to her happiness in the palm of her hand. Being here made everything that had happened the week before lighter, easier.

She wanted to hope, but she was too scared. Hope felt like a cheating wife, coming in to give Rio some relief and then escaping, as sneakily as she entered, leaving Rio fucked and ruined.

Agatha let out a soft snore and snuggled further into Rio’s arms and Rio tightened her hold on her. For now, she had this. She refused to go back to sleep, instead, played with the ends of Agatha’s hair mindlessly as she imagined what it would be to do this every morning.

She really wished that she hadn’t lost the chance to do this forever.

Eventually, the alarm rang. Rio made no move to silence it, hoping to stay in this moment, hoping if she ignored it enough it would just stop. Eventually, Agatha’s eyes shot open and she reached over Rio to turn it off. When she pulled back from the nightstand, she seemed to realize how close they were and blushed.

“Sorry,” she mumbled.

“‘Tis okay,” Rio said, instead of her preferred response of come back here.

Agatha got up and scooted off, picking up her phone and running into the bathroom. Rio lazily stretched, disappointed but not surprised this ended the way it did.

Agatha just wanted to be friends. And Rio would respect the hell out of that, no matter what she personally wanted.

She was not going to take more than Agatha was comfortable with giving.

She had taken too much already.

Rio opened her phone hoping for a distraction and she got one. There were a few panicked texts from Jen so Rio just decided to call her.

“Rio!” Jen said, picking up after a few rings. “Is Agatha around?”

Agatha chose that moment to walk out of the bathroom, hair still disheveled, the black floral robe she adored over her clothes.

“Yeah, she is,” Rio said, gesturing to Agatha to come back into the bed and putting the phone on speaker. “You’re on speaker.”

“Agatha, I know you are still hurt, but the Hospital Gala event is tonight,” Jen’s voice crackled into the studio.

“Oh shit, I totally forgot about that.” Agatha sighed as she sat down on the edge of the bed.

“See, the thing is I would tell you not to come at all, but it is literally in tandem with Westview Presbyterian and our bosses would really like to celebrate you and have you speak about both our company and the care you got at the hospital.”

Rio scoffed. “Care? Let me tell you something about the care Agatha got--”

“Rio,” Agatha cut her off, placing a hand on her shoulder and rubbing slow circles, a gesture that made Rio’s heart stop. “Jen, I don’t know if I can do this. I’m still not ready to come back to work full time.”

“I get it Ags, I just thought this would be a good moment to show your face to everyone, make a speech and then immediately leave and not worry about work for another few weeks. Because otherwise they will make you come to the bug emporium benefit in two weeks.”

“Oh god, no, yeah. I don’t want to do that.” She sighed. “Fuck, you are right. I think tonight might be the move.”

“Are you sure?” Rio asked and Agatha turned to face her, blue eyes looking into Rio’s so deeply she thought she would drown.

“I’m sure, if it's only for an hour or so, I will be okay.”

“Okay, great you and Rio can--”

“Rio? No, I will be fine on my own.”

“Yeah, I am not letting you go to this event alone,” Rio grumbled, tensing up.

Agatha looked surprised as if she didn’t already predict that Rio was going to come with her. “Rio, I don’t need a babysitter--”

Jen’s voice crackled through the phone. “Actually, about that, um, Agatha you might want to bring a date. Ralph has been, um, saying things about--”

“I don’t need to know,” Agatha cut in, eyes narrowing. “I feel like I have a very good idea of what Ralph has been saying about me.”

“Who’s Ralph?” Rio couldn’t help but ask.

Agatha looked away and mumbled something incoherent.

“Who’s Ralph?” Rio repeated, louder.

“He is this guy who works with us and he’s kind of, um, obsessed with Agatha,” Jen replied.

Obsessed?

Rio was going to rip him limb from limb.

“I’m sorry, why is this the first I have heard of this?”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “Because of this exact reason. You cannot hurt him, Rio. He is the nephew of the head of the company.”

“So, the PR firm will get a new nephew. Big deal, can you tell me his full name, Jen?”

“As much as I would enjoy this, Agatha is right. But there is something you may be able to do,” Jen murmured. Rio should have recognized the smugness in her voice for the blaring red signal it was.

“You two should come together.”

“Yeah, we are obviously--”

“No, you guys should come as a couple.”

Silence. Rio heard something fall in the distance. Probably the other shoe.

“I’m sorry?” Agatha strangled out. “You want us to--what?”

“Jen, what the hell are you saying?” Rio’s heart was beating wildly.

“I’m saying you two numbnuts should fake-date each other for one night so Ralph leaves Agatha alone forever, because let’s face it, Rio is scary.”

Fake date a girl she is in love with? This seems stupid even for Rio.

“Why me? Why not Wanda? Aren’t you two a--”

“Nothing happened between me and Wanda,” Agatha said softly. “We are nothing but friends.”

Jen sighed. “And I’m asking you, Rio, because you will go all fierce protector on Agatha all night and not leave her side and then bring her home anyway so you both are literally halfway there. All you have to do is sell it a little.”

Agatha looked like she was caught between blind panic and hysteria. “What about Nat? She won’t be okay with this, would she?”

“Uh, Nat and I--”

“Nat isn’t a problem.” Jen said confidently. “I talked to her this morning, she is all okay with this.”

“You talked to Nat this morning?” Rio almost screeched. “Why? Is everything okay?”

“Rio, you really need to call her back.” Rio could hear the laughter in her voice.

“Fuck, I know. I have been kind of trying to avoid that part but she has been texting me everyday with updates about insurance and everything else so I think I am pretty in the loop.” Rio was smiling as she turned to Agatha who looked like she had seen a ghost.

“Agatha?” Rio questioned, reaching out but before she could touch her, Agatha flinched.

“I don’t know if it is a good idea to do this.”

“Agatha--” Rio started only to be cut off.

“Think of it this way. One night and you will be rid of two problems and you two can go back to whatever you’re doing and your bunny.” Jen said

Agatha tapped her chin like she was considering it. “Fuck it, if everyone is okay with it, yeah.”

“Are you sure?” Rio questioned, searching Agatha for any discomfort.

Agatha nodded and got up, moving to Scratchy’s pen and lifting him up. “Yeah, one night and then everything goes back to normal.” Agatha seemed a little choked up, but Rio assumed it was from Scratchy fur getting in her eyes.

“Okay, great. I will see you both at five,” Jen said and hung up.

“Are you sure?” Rio asked, no harm in triple-checking or quadruple-checking too.

“Are you sure?” Agatha asked, eyes heavy with an emotion Rio couldn’t place.

Rio nodded mindlessly. Anything for you.

“You should get ready at yours,” Agatha said a few moments later.

Don’t ask me to go. “Why?”

Agatha tilted her head, looking at her as if she was stupid. “Because all your stuff is there?”

Oh, yeah.

That is how Rio ended up at her apartment for the first time in two weeks. Her plants were alive, thanks in large part to Lilia, but everything else was covered in a thin layer of dust.

She had a long bath, possibly the first real one since Agatha got hurt. She rinsed off the crusted sweat and dried tears that had found their permanent place in her skin, hoping they would take all the feelings that had weighed on her soul with them.

She loved Agatha, she knew that, but there was a loud voice that constantly reminded her that she didn’t deserve Agatha.

Not after she spent ten years violently suppressing her feelings for her. Letting them build. Letting them rot. They had turned into mangled versions of themselves, carrying weight that would not have been saddled if she had simply let herself feel.

But she didn’t.

Because it was easier to admit they had nothing than it was to watch Agatha know and choose someone else.

It was easier to laugh and joke about it because talking about it would wreck her.

It was easier to run away than it was to know she would be rejected.

But it wasn’t fair. It wasn’t fair to Agatha and it wasn’t fair to her.

Because Rio never let herself truly accept it or let it go. It always hung between them, a possibility, a future she was too scared to ask for.

She didn’t want to end up like her parents.

She couldn’t end up like her parents. Full of anger that consumed all their good parts, full of disdain and torment. How could you end up hating the person you love?

Could she end up hating Agatha?

No. But she could end up hating herself.

Fuck, she already did.

There was not one relationship she had not thrown a live grenade into when she was scared of being abandoned, not one shred of happiness that stayed once she brought out the machine guns and let them loose on herself, not one future that she didn’t rip apart with her own bare hands.

Because she didn’t deserve happiness.

And she sure as hell didn’t deserve Agatha.

But for the first time in her life, Rio wanted to try to be worthy.

Rio wanted to unleash all the love that had been building up inside her. No matter how many compartments and files and boxes she found in her mind to stash, hide, burn the love she had to Agatha, it came pouring back the second she looked into those blue eyes.

Because she was like the Titanic in that way, no matter how many compartments and buffer rooms she created out of thin air when she hit the fatal iceberg, the love still seeped in, filling, sinking, engulfing her until there was nothing but the soft tune of the orchestra and a million drowned reasons she shouldn’t do this.

And Rio was really tired of trying to claw her way back to the surface.

So, for possibly the first time in her adult life, she let herself feel.

And she let it all out. Everything she had bottled up. All the pain that was gnawing at her.

Of seeing Agatha in that fucking hospital room, attached to monitors, fighting through pain, not being able to do anything, not being able to help, not be able to tell her how much she is loved.
Of watching her walk away time after time, not saying anything, trying not to feel anything, a prison of her own making.

Of loving someone and only getting crumbs. Being able to kiss her on the cheek but not on the mouth. Being able to be there for her constantly, but not being able to be there in the way that mattered.

And she loved Agatha so much.

She loved how Agatha was fearless and strong and never took no for an answer. She loved how Agatha blushed when you made an inappropriate joke but tried to mask it under a cough. She loved how she thought about the world, as if it was both beautiful and broken at the same time, but never let the ugliness eat her from within, never let her past define who she was.

But a part of that love was respect. And Agatha had made it very clear that she only looked at Rio as a friend.

Rio knew Agatha cared. Agatha clearly cared.

She ate Rio’s food even though the spices were too much and her eyes would water and she would cough. She secretly researched all of Rio’s hyperfixations and interests so they could talk about it together. She would keep all of Rio’s half finished projects as mementos.

Fuck, she even seemed to only be watching telenovelas lately, as though she knew had been trying to get better by watching the shows. She knew Rio didn’t know how to speak Spanish but still understood it and was struggling with that fact. Rio swore she caught Agatha twice in the bathroom practising how to speak Spanish, even though she violently denied it.

And Agatha had taken every protection bracelet and new diet and smelly paste Rio had thrown at her, never once telling Rio that her worry was too much, never once making her feel like she wasn’t wanted.

I think I know what you are going to say, and I just can’t do that right now, Rio.

Agatha cared and loved Rio as a friend.

And that is a fact she was going to get used to. She knew she would never fully move on, but she owed to herself and Agatha to give what she could until Agatha didn’t want it anymore.

Can we just go back to being Rio and Agatha, best friends forever?

Rio was tired of running and hiding and drowning. She was going to feel it all, all the love, all the rejection, all the fucking pain.

I need my best friend back.

She was going to stop hiding and face the music head on.

She loved Agatha Harkness and she wasn't afraid of it anymore.
