Chapter 14

Chapter Summary

agatha finds doubts and answers

Chapter Notes

rollercoaster alert (i am sorry)!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness was going to cry.

Her dress was not fitting over her boot, her goddamn hair looked like a rat’s nest and she ran out of concealer.

She was so ready to call this entire thing off when she heard Rio shuffle in, and she walked out, hair frizzy, makeup half on, a makeshift bib tucked into her collar and froze.

Because there stood Rio in a very sharp suit, black with little gray pinstripes running down, the collar plunging dangerously low, no shirt to hide the curve of her cleavage, and lips stained red.

As if Agatha wasn’t already having visceral visions of flinging her against walls when she was in shark pajamas.

Her heart really couldn’t handle this.

“You look beautiful,” Rio said, smiling wide and genuine.

“Don’t lie to me, I look like a kid just threw up on me,” Agatha rolled her eyes. Rio stuck her tongue in her cheek, trying not to laugh.

Breathe, you idiot. Fucking breathe.

“Let me help,” she said, grabbing her hairbrush and gently coming to stand behind her, combing her hair softly.

Rio looked so damn cute, eyes scrunched, focused.

Agatha had the desire to do something very stupid.

Something she probably shouldn’t do considering the last time she had this desire she threw a live grenade into their relationship.

“Rio?” Idiot, idiot, don’t do it. Rio looked up anyway.

“Why have you done all this for me? You’ve never been this,” she paused, trying to find the right word, “involved.”

Rio looked gutted. Agatha swore she saw her eyes glisten.

“I never thought you’d let me.”

Agatha’s heart lurched.

Rio paused and Agatha thought this was all she was going to get. She was wrong.

“I’ve always thought I didn’t deserve you so I held back, gave less, hid more. But sometimes things happen that make you realize that life is too short. I don’t want to live like this forever.” Rio took a deep breath.

Agatha’s eyes shone. “What do you want to live like?”

“I want to be better. I want to love louder and live freer, away from the worry, away from the fear. I want to be worthy.”

Agatha’s heart broke a little.

“Rio, you are worthy,” she said, finding her eyes in the mirror.

Rio scoffed and shook her head. “I am not, but it is okay. I will spend my entire life trying to be worthy of you.”

Agatha’s eyes widened and she stared into Rio’s eyes. This felt dangerously close to a confession.

They didn’t do confessions.

But, maybe they should.

“I don’t think I am enough either. I don’t think I am good. I don’t think I get to be happy.”

Rio’s eyes softened. “Agatha, of all the people in the entire world, you are the only person I know who deserves it more than everyone.”

“You’re just biased,” Agatha said, not stopping the slow smile that took over her face.

“Yeah,” Rio replied, smiling too. “I am.”

They piled into the car five minutes later, silence descending over the car as the sun set in the distance, but this time, it was a bit lighter, a bit more companionable.

More intimate.

When they arrived, Rio ran over, opening the car door before Agatha could even try. They walked up in silence, not touching, but close enough that a small movement would cause them to.

“Ready?” Rio asked, turning to face Agatha in front of the entrance.

“Ready,” Agatha nodded.

Rio held her arm out to her. “Tonight you're mine,” she murmured under breath softly. So softly Agatha almost missed it.

Her heart started beating widely.

The Gala had just started as they entered, tall tables scattered around a large ballroom, waiters flicking between tables with trays of food, elegant decorations and flowers hanging all around.

“Agatha!”

Already? Ralph wasted no fucking time. He was already by her side, leaning over to hug her when he was yanked backwards.

“I’m sorry, who are you?” Rio growled, holding the back of his collar.

“I’m Ralph Bohner,” he said proudly, raising his nose towards Rio. “I’m pretty important here. Who the hell are you?”

“I’m the girlfriend of the woman you just tried to hug. Here’s a piece of advice, don’t try again.” Rio’s eyes burned with anger and something that felt a lot like possession.

Tonight you're mine. Mine.

It rang through Agatha’s head like a broken bell, loud and deep, filling every available corner.

Mine. Mine. Mine.

“I didn’t know she was dating someone,” Ralph was sweating. Rio brought herself close again, draping her arm around Agatha.

“Now you know, so can you stop bothering her or shall I find HR?”

“Nope, no, not again. I am gonna go, have a good night you two,” Ralph ran out.

The second he left, Rio dropped her hand, face relaxing.

“Well, that’s over. Now we just have to get through your speech and enjoy the night.”

“Yeah, where is the bar--”

Agatha froze as she came in contact with the one pair of eyes she thought she would never see again.

“Agatha.” That voice haunted her dreams.

“Mother.”

She was in many ways the same and very different. Same pale skin stretched out over sharp bones, but now her brown hair was fully white, and those emotionless eyes, frantic.

“What are you doing here?” Agatha tried her best to sound brave.

“I am a donor of the hospital,” Evanora replied, a cold mask descending.

“In Westview?”

“It is owned by a trust that deals with many hospitals all along the east coast.” Cold. Harsh.

Like Agatha was stupid for not knowing. Like Agatha was a fool.

“Can we talk alone?” Evanora asked, almost dismissively.

Rio moved in front of Agatha, arms crossed, teeth bared, blocking her from Evanora’s view. Like a guard dog. “No.”

“Rio,” Agatha said, shaking her head. Her eyes pleaded with Rio. No violence today. “You get exactly ten minutes.”

Rio moved aside, arms still crossed, jaw set as she walked away, still within pouncing distance but out of earshot.

“So, what do you want?” Agatha asked, whipping forward, knowing there was some angle, some thing Evanora needed from her.

“Do I need to want something to see you?”

“Yes.”

“I just wanted to, you know, catch up.” Evanora said, sounding too eager, well as eager as a heartless bitch can sound.

Agatha narrowed her eyes.

“What are you doing with your life, Agatha?” Evanora finally said, arms raised, knife in hand ready to eviscerate Agatha’s emotions. “Is this all worth leaving your family over? Your mother over?”

“I didn’t leave you,” Agatha said, refusing to show any weakness. “You disowned me.”

“You did this to yourself. I see you, Agatha.” Evanora said, bracing for attack, eyes sharp, mouth curled in a feline smirk. “You and I are the same.”

“No, we are not.” Agatha’s confidence was wavering. She was literally confronted by her worst fear.

“Are we not? Because from where I am standing I see you alone, unloved, unworthy. All the things you swore I was all those years ago.”

“I am not--” Agatha began. But Evanora had sunk her blade right between Agatha’s chest and she was determined to rip her daughter to shreds.

“You are alone. You are no good. Everyone around you can see it. See that you are wicked.”

“I am not wicked.” Agatha said, but her voice was wavering.

Evanora saw that for what it was, an opening. “No one will ever love you. No one can. You are unloveable.”

“I am not,” Agatha said, almost pleading. “I have my friends. I have my-- Rio.”

“Your Rio, huh? And where is your Rio?”

Agatha looked towards the house and locked eyes with Rio who was now next to Wanda and Nat.

Nat.

She forgot about Nat.

She forgot that Rio wasn’t hers.

She forgot this was all fake.

“Oh, I remember her,” Evanora said, following Agatha’s gaze. “She’s your charity case. The friend she brought around everywhere, like your own personal bitch.”

Rage tore through Agatha at those words. “You have no right to talk to her like that--”

“Why are you so angry, Agatha,” Evanora said, narrowing her eyes and connecting the dots Agatha absolutely did not want her to connect. “Is it because you love her?”

Agatha said nothing, still staring at Rio, watching her whisper worriedly with their friends, still trying to build up her walls that had been completely destroyed by her mother.

“You do, don’t you? And let me guess, she doesn’t love you back.”

And with that Evanora tore open all the wounds Agatha had so painfully stitched together, pouring salt into the bleeding gash, watching as blood poured out of her daughter and grinning with joy.

Because she was right. Rio didn’t love her.

No matter how much she tried to pretend she did, with this blissful week they just spent and the taking care of her, no matter how much she wished it to be true, Rio didn’t look at her that way.

She didn’t want to be her girlfriend.

She didn’t want to be with her at all.

Hell, she didn’t fucking visit her in the hospital.

Because that is what it came down to, that is what it all came down to, Rio wasn’t there when Agatha needed her the most.

“You know I am right,” Evanora said. “Come back with me. Come back home and run the firm, I’m getting old, I need a successor.”

Agatha turned away, tears blinding her vision. She heard a crash and then aggressive stomping but she couldn’t really process anything.

Because for once her mother was right.

Evanora was an awful, horrid human but a broken clock is right twice a day, and unfortunately, she was very right about this.

She was not loved by the one person she wanted. And it was killing her.

The next thing she knew multiple people were pulling Rio off her mother as Evanora yelled bloody murder.

“She broke my nose, the bitch, I’m going to sue her, I’m going to sue all of you.”

“I’d like to see you try,” Rio yelled back, fury engulfing her face.

Agatha should have felt triumphant that Rio defended her but all that was beating in her heart was she doesn’t love you, she never will. You will never be good enough. You will always be evil.

“Rio,” Agatha said. Because that is all she could in that moment. “Stop.”

She didn’t visit you in the hospital. She will leave you. She will never love you.

Rio immediately stopped, fighting away from her friend’s grasps and walking towards Agatha.

The thing about the other shoe is that Agatha is that never waits for it to fall. She would rather rip it out violently on her own terms than be blindsided.

“Are you okay?” Rio asked, voice alarmed.

“I’m unpausing.”

“Unpausing what?”

“I don’t want you here. I don’t want you in my life.”

Rio’s eyes melted into shock, her mouth falling open. “Agatha, what?”

“I want you to leave me alone.”

“But we-- but I-- what?”

“I never want to see your face again.”

“Agatha, I don’t understand what happened, we were fine-- we--”

“You never visited me in the hospital. You let me fucking rot there alone. You weren’t there when I needed you, Rio, did you think I would just forget that?”

“I never left-- Agatha, what is happening?” Rio was pleading.

Agatha stormed off, behind her mother, Rio trailing.

“Agatha, can we please talk this, you don’t know the full story--”

“Have your stuff out of my house before I come back.”

Agatha barely made it into the bathroom before the tears found her.

She was gutted, devastated.

No, devastated would be the wrong word. What is the word for when your mother drudges up all your past fears and throws them on your face and you realize the love of your life doesn’t love you and you tell them you never want to see them again even though you want the exact opposite and now you’ve broken your own heart and your bunny is now a child of divorce? That word, that word is what she is feeling.

Agatha was too caught up in making sure no one could hear her cry, shoving her fist into her mouth while her tears ran loose when she heard giggles and moans and a voice.

A very familiar voice.

“Baby, I missed you, fuck. We need to be quiet.”

Nat.

She could hear sporadic kissing, getting more heated with the moment. Fuck, Rio wasted no time, did she?

“But you make it so hard, baby.”

It wasn’t Rio who said it, no, it was Wanda.

“Wanda, we can’t, not here,” Nat said between moans.

What the fuck? Was this bitch cheating on Rio? Agatha was going to gut her like a fish.

“Why not?” Wanda whined.

“Well, for starters, my ex is here.”

Ex? Ex? They weren’t together?

“Rio wouldn’t mind.” Wanda said, and Agatha could hear a zipper being opened. “She would want you to move on considering she is literally moved in with Agatha.”

What the fuck. What the fuck. What the fuck.

“We just broke up, Wanda.”

Wanda sighed. “Your relationship lasted like four days.”

Rio and Nat broke up? After only four days? That doesn’t make sense.

That doesn’t make sense.

Because it meant that they were broken up the day Agatha got hit by the car.

But she saw them. She saw them laughing.

Friends laugh, a voice said in her head, fuck. Rio wasn’t with Nat.

“She seems so sad and miserable.”

“Well, that is their fault. If they can’t see what is right in front of them then it’s their fault.”

It couldn’t be.

“We have to stop.’

Wanda sighed heavier. “I know.”

The door slammed shut. She was alone again.

What the fuck just happened.

Rio wasn’t with Nat. Rio didn’t have a girlfriend. Rio was single.

Agatha wanted to scream. Or cry. Or probably both. Hysterically. Uncontrollably.

She remembered what it felt like to wake up this morning. In Rio’s arms.

Agatha had slowly opened her eyes, feeling warm and content and snuggled into her pillow for a moment. And then she felt something moving right next to her. Her eyes shot open as she took in their new position, suddenly losing sleep altogether as she found that she was curled over Rio’s chest and her face was in Rio’s neck.

Agatha wondered how she would get out of there without waking Rio. And then she felt it.

Rio was playing with her hair. Not just playing, no, twisting and curling and lazing around, wide awake and not bothered that Agatha was in her arms.

Agatha almost cried.

The alarm blared next to them but Rio didn’t loosen her grip on Agatha and Agatha did not know what to do with this piece of information.

The alarm got louder and louder but Rio just lay there. Agatha did too, ignoring it, willing it away, but the sound of the alarm finally got too much. She reached over Rio to stop it.

When she pulled back a little she could see Rio staring at her with the biggest, most beautiful brown eyes.

I want to kiss her, Agatha thought.

Instead she bolted to the bathroom.

But Rio was single. She could have kissed her. She threw a live grenade into her life for no reason.

Rio was single.

She needed to get out of here. She needed air. She needed Rio.

She tore out of the venue, tears blazing, no worry about her broken leg, no worry about anything.

Pain seared up her leg as she hugged a street light outside, collapsing against the weight of it.

She needed to tell Rio she was jealous. She needed to apologize. She couldn’t run home? Could she? Fuck Rio was taking all her stuff out of the room.

But just because Rio is single doesn’t mean she loves you, a voice whispered in her head.

“Agatha, is that you?”

Agatha knew that voice, she just didn’t know from where.

“Agatha?” called the same voice. A face came into view, blurry behind her tears.

“Nurse Danvers?”

“I thought it was you,” Nurse Danvers said, rounding over to her and giving her a hug. “How are you? Where are your crutches?”

“Uh, I don’t know.”

“Oh, is everything okay?” The nurse looked at Agatha with concern, taking in her swollen eyes and running makeup.

Agatha nodded. Then shook her head.

“Where is Rio?”

“She is-- uh, she is--” Agatha choked, then a realization dawned on her. “Wait, how do you know Rio?”

“What do you mean, Agatha? Of course I know Rio,” Nurse Danvers chuckled. “When someone doesn’t leave the emergency room for five days, you tend to learn their name.”

Agatha’s head snapped up. “What?”

“Oh, you are so lucky to have someone who loves you like that,” Nurse Danvers said, almost swooning.

“She didn’t leave the hospital for days?” Agatha’s tongue felt like it was on fire, her eyes were stinging with tears again.

“No,” Nurse Danvers said, ushering Agatha to sit on one of the benches near them. She placed a hand on her knee “Sweetie, are you okay?”

“Can you please tell me exactly what she did when she was there? Every last detail?” Agatha was trying to push away the feeling in her chest that felt like she was being pushed underwater.

“She came in as you got admitted into the hospital and didn’t leave until you left with her. I think she left once to grab some stuff from your house, I think, but she spent every waking hour begging anyone who would listen for updates about you and traumatizing poor Doctor Banner with questions about your medications and treatment plans. And oh-- when she found you you might be going in withdrawal, she almost threw Doctor Banner off a ledge. She got William assigned to spend the night with you. I still remember her saying something very romantic along the lines of ‘She's the love of my life, kid, don’t let anything happen to her,’ because William cried about it for a week.”

The love of her life?

She couldn’t breathe. It felt like her heart was being pumped into her body and ripped at the same time.

Rio wasn’t dating anyone.

Rio held her through her worst nights.

Rio took care of their bunny and her and bought her protection bracelets and held her in her sleep.

She called her the love of her life.

“She said I was the love of her life?” Agatha whispered.

“Oh, she said much more than that whenever she sat with you.”

“She sat with me?” Agatha spluttered.

“Oh, every night, sweetheart. She would hold your hand and kiss it all night long.”

Rio sat by her bedside, Rio never left the hospital, Rio nursed her back to health.

“I-- I need to go.”

Rio didn’t leave her, she didn’t abandon her. Could she hope?

Could she hope Rio loved her as much as she loved Rio?

Agatha feral barked at the Uber driver the entire way home, traumatizing him within an inch of his life.

She's the love of my life, kid, don’t let anything happen to her, echoed in her head repeatedly, a hope, a prayer.

Please don’t leave, she chanted in her head. Please don’t be gone before I get to say I love you too.

WE ARE FINALLY GETTING PLACES!

Chapter 15

Chapter Summary

so um progress?

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio Vidal was not sure what the fuck just happened.

Everything was fine until Evanora Harkness showed up.

I don’t want you here.

Why Agatha chose to talk to her mother, Rio will never know. But she did.

I don’t want you in my life.

Why did Rio punch her? Well, it was clear that Evanora was making Agatha cry.

Have your stuff out of my house before I come back.

Now was the reason enough for Agatha to tell her to fuck off? Yes.

But did she actually expect to hear those words again?

I never want to see your face again.

No, she did not.

Honestly, she was a fool. A fool for believing she was forgiven at all. Because if she was Agatha, she wouldn’t forgive her either.

Agatha stormed away. Rio stood still.

Her friends around her spoke but she couldn’t make out words.

Breathe in.

“Rio, Rio?”

Breathe out.

“What the hell happened?”

Breathe in.

“Where is Agatha going?”

Breathe out.

“Rio, what did you do?” Lilia said, next to her, staring at Evanora, her broken nose and the donors that crowded around her in the corner.

“I think Agatha and I are done for real this time.” Rio finally said, words harsh in her throat.

“What the hell?” Jen yelled near her.

Rio was walking away, she could feel her feet taking her outside. She leaned back against the wall. Air whipped around her face. She could feel the walls come up, she could feel herself build back her cages.

This was just like her parents, with their anger and fear and festering, bleeding each other dry, refusing to leave, refusing to stay.

How did they get here?

Her parents always yelled, always tore each other to shreds, always found what made the other person hurt and pressed.

Is that what she and Agatha did to each other?

They were different, but in many ways, they were the same.

They didn’t listen, they didn’t talk, they spent a lifetime living in between mumbled words and stolen glances, begging the other person to read their mind, forever trapped in the area between uncertainty and freedom.

Breathe in.

She didn’t want to be like her parents. She didn’t want Agatha to be the scar she wore for life.

Breathe out.

She had nothing to lose. Agatha was already stubbornly marching her way out of her life. She was already losing her.

Breathe in.

It was time for her to do something brave. Something very brave.

Breathe out.

Because Victoria Vidal was something, for sure.

A hurricane, tornado, black hole.

Something that sucked all the attention around it, leaving room for nothing else.

(Between you and I, they were, most definitely, screwed.)

Chapter Summary

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio Vidal was hyperventilating.

She couldn’t seem to catch her breath, it was always running away just as she got close to catching up.

She couldn’t seem to tamp down her thoughts, wild and rabid, tearing open wounds she was very sure she had stapled shut.

Very luckily for her, it didn’t seem to freeze her, no, it seemed to make her a machine.

She stripped the sheets off the bed, threw on fresh sheets, tucked in the duvet and arranged the million plush throw pillows Agatha had bought at Bed, Bath and Beyond in the same amount of time it took Agatha to place an UberEats order for grocery delivery.

She scrubbed the bathtub with vigor, attacking the toilet while the bleach rested, and then polished all the taps and showerheads until they shone, cleaning every crevice while Agatha moved Scratchy and his cage to their room.

When groceries were delivered, she all but grabbed them out of the poor delivery guy’s hands, beginning to arrange them in the fridge even before the door fully closed.

“I’m beginning to understand why the people in the hospital were scared of you,” Agatha joked when she walked out and watched Rio shove an entire bunch of carrots into an already very full vegetable drawer.

No response. Rio was focused on winning the war against the freezer.

A sigh. “Baby, you need to slow down.”

Nope.

Rio needed to go faster.

Rio finished shelving the groceries and moved on to their bedroom, stripping their sheets and throwing them in the laundry.

“Baby, those sheets are clean,” Agatha said, leaning on the door frame as Rio zoomed around the room.

“Not clean enough,” Rio grumbled, stripping off the mattress topper too, “They still smell like sex.”

Agatha smirked, “Who’s fault is that?”

Fine, Rio ate her out this morning. She was hungry.

Sue her.

Rio didn’t acknowledge Agatha’s comment with anything external, choosing instead to tear open a spare pack of sheets they kept on the highest shelf in their closet and start to tuck it into the corners of the mattress. Agatha joined in on the other end, helping Rio in silence.

Once they were done, Rio moved on to the drawers, rearranging and folding haphazardly thrown in clothes and finally, pulling the drawer with all the fun toys out.

“What are you doing?” Agatha asked, arms crossed.

“Hiding the straps,” Rio said casually, putting all of the toys in the appropriate cloth bags, “Can you find me an empty shoebox?”

“Rio. They’re already in a drawer,” Agatha remarked.

Rio scoffed and shook her head.

“Agatha, my mother is going to stick her head in every crevice of this house and unless you’re okay with her finding our toy drawer and all the questions that would come with it, we need to put them all in a box and, just to be safe, burn them.”

“I don’t have time for this,” Rio clawed out of her embrace. “I love you and whatever, but we need to finish cleaning.”

Rio would apologize, later.

Because in less than five minutes, her mother would be standing in this apartment.

And Rio was holding a silicone dick.

“No,” Agatha said firmly, “No.”

“Fine, I’ll use another box,” Rio said, doubling back and placing the shoes back in the box with as much care she could at that moment and opening one of her own shoeboxes.

“Rio,” Agatha said, grabbing her arm. “We’re not doing this… you can’t shut me out.”

Rio tried not to flinch. It felt like Agatha’s touch was burning her skin.

Rio pulled out of her hold, head down, kept going. “I’m not shutting you out, Agatha. I’m saving both of us from uncomfortable questions.”

“Why won’t you look at me?” Agatha all but screamed.

Rio blinked.

Paused.

Looked up at Agatha and then:

“I know you’re not stupid, Agatha,” Rio scrunched up her face. “So, why are you choosing this moment to pick a fight?”

“You’ve been ignoring me since you found out your mother was coming,” Agatha wrapped her arms around her middle. “Don’t invalidate my feelings.”

Agatha stared at her, eyes shining.

Rio internally cringed and opened her mouth again with a reluctant apology, when:

There was a knock on the door.

Rio froze, locking eyes with Agatha, fear surging through her veins.

Another knock. More impatient.

Rio couldn’t move.

She was stuck, captive, bound to that spot.

It was happening.

She was here.

She was going to ruin everything.

She was going to show Agatha how broken Rio was.

A series of knocks. Very impatient.

Rio had to stop this.

Had to stop her.

She looked up towards Agatha, emotion coursing through her eyes.

Rio wanted to shake her.

How typical.

Her mom always did this, glazed over everything that was important to Rio. Well, usually until a certain someone was mentioned.

A clear trap.

Agatha took a sharp breath in.

Don’t respond. Don’t respond. Rio chanted in her head.

“Yes,” Rio said, unhesitantly.

Victoria just rolled her eyes.

Low blow.

Rio sighed.

In some ways, what she said was worse.

Those words, the way it was levied, this exact conversation, it reminded Rio of the one thing she dreaded the most.

They were becoming her parents.

Same bite, same hunger, trying to maul each other before the other one can.

She couldn’t breathe.

The walls were closing in.

“I need to go,” Rio said, heart beating wildly. “I need to go.”

She couldn’t breathe.

Maybe her mother was right.

Maybe she was Death reincarnated.

Maybe she did kill everything she touched.

Somehow, she hoped it was different this time.

Different with Agatha.

She burst out the front door and ran into the night, running where she didn’t know, just as long as it was far from here.

Far from home.

Was this it?

Were they doomed from the start?

What had they come to?

Chapter 24

Chapter Summary

Agatha Harkness truly believed it was all going to be okay.

Why wouldn’t it be?

Victoria Vidal was always an elusive figure in Agatha’s life.

They had met a handful of times, college graduation, Rio’s birthdays, occasional visits, but nothing longer than passing pleasantries, nothing that would truly allow Agatha to judge her character.

So, Agatha always saw her through Rio’s eyes: an equal mix of judgement and pain, loving her mother, being grateful for her but wanting nothing more than to escape her purview.

Personally, Agatha never understood the last part.

Rio’s parents were always there for her. Messy and erratic, but present. They called each other once a week. They sent her money when times were hard. They sent flowers on important occasions. They listened to her aspirations and dreams and they pushed her towards greater things.

They weren’t the best, but they were there.

Which was more than Agatha could say about her parents.

Agatha’s father was a distant memory, a blur that swept through her mind at times. Even though he passed when she was in college, he was never really there.

He went about life as if he was alone. Work, eat, sleep, work, eat, sleep, work, eat, sleep until he died.

Evanora, on the other hand, was too present.

Hell bent on shaping her only child in her image.

She was too particular. Too discerning. Like a flash of lightning, sharp, tight, blinding.

And Agatha was never enough.

Not popular enough. Not smart enough. Not pretty enough.

Hell, she wasn’t even good enough at chores.

Every time Evanora would come home from work, she’d tear through the house, fixing all of Agatha’s ‘mistakes,’ ripping things out of the dishwasher, refolding her clothes, remaking the bed, all seemingly casual, but Agatha knew they were taunts.

They were punishments.

I don’t think I am good.

I don’t think I get to be happy.

I don’t think I am enough either.

So why was Rio acting like she was?

She looked scared.

No, she looked terrified.

Deep breaths, Agatha told herself.

This is not about you.

Another knock. More impatient.

Rio didn’t move.

This is not about you. Agatha chanted in her head.

This is about Rio.

A series of knocks. Very impatient.

Rio looked up towards Agatha, so much emotion coursing through her eyes.

Agatha could fix this.

Agatha needed to fix this.

Agatha snapped into action, rushing over to the door and unlocking it with the best smile on her face.

Deep breaths. Deep breaths.

“Victoria,” she said cheerfully, flashing a big smile.

Victoria Vidal stood at the other end, soft brown hair tied up in a messy ponytail, dressed in a colorful mismatch of patterns and shapes, white skin shining with a flush of someone who just heaved themselves up the stairs.

“Do I have the right apartment?” Victoria said, head tilted in emotion. Agatha blinked back at the lack of recognition.

“Rio?”

Rio appeared behind her, draping her arm firmly around Agatha’s waist.

Agatha leaned into the contact. Trying to ground herself.

It was all going to be okay.

“Hi, mom,” Rio said, firmly. “You’ve met Agatha before, haven’t you.”

“Oh, yes,” Victoria said enthusiastically, pulling Agatha into a big, sweeping hug, “Of course, I remember you. Rio’s best friend, right? You’ve changed so much. Last time I saw you was so much younger. What was it? Almost ten years ago!”

Agatha tried shaking off her words.

Best foot forward.

“Yes, at graduation, how are you—” Agatha said, smiling apprehensively as Victoria pulled away and launched herself at Rio.

It was all okay. It was all okay. It was all okay.

Victoria loved Rio, that was for sure.

“This is such a nice place you have, Rio,” Victoria giggled, letting Rio go so she could prance over to fiddle with the coffee table decor.

Breathe in and let it roll off your back.

“Thank you, mom,” Rio trailed after her, “It was all Agatha.”

Breathe out and be thankful for your girlfriend.

“How sweet of Agatha to decorate your place,” Victoria nodded as she looked out the window, noting their outdoor furniture. “Why do you have fake grass on your terrace?”

Breathe in and try not to bash your own head in.

Agatha walked up next to Rio.

Breathe out and try not to kill your future mother-in-law.

She looked so soft and terrified and Agatha wanted to wrap herself around her and never let her go.

It was all going to be okay.

Agatha sighed, allowing her heart to fill with joy again, and pulled her girlfriend in, snaking her arm around her waist and leaving a soft kiss on her temple.

Somehow that helped both of them.

“She’s my girlfriend, mom,” Rio snapped. “If you don’t respect that, there is the door.”

Agatha froze.

Rio was being so combative.

Didn’t she know, didn’t she know her mother could hurt her?

She had to protect Rio.

She had to protect herself.

Victoria huffed, crossing her arms. “You’re so emotional, Rio. Can’t even make a joke around you. It was supposed to be funny,” Victoria rolled her eyes.

Too emotional.

Agatha tried inhaling, but the air had left the room.

“You’re not funny, mom.”

She was almost choking.

“Agatha thought it was funny, didn’t she?” Victoria smirked.

A clear trap.

Agatha took a sharp breath in.

She was fucked either way.

She coughed, moving to sit and weakly saying, “Sure.”

“See!” Victoria triumphed. She drew back and pointed her finger at Rio, “You’d throw your own mother out on the street?”

“Yes,” Rio said, unhesitantly.

Does she have a fucking death wish?

Does Rio want to be bitch-slapped?

Victoria just rolled her eyes.

What the fuck.

What the fuck.

How is Rio alive?

“Why are you here, mom?” Rio moved to face her mother on the couch, “What happened?”

“So, are you two serious?” Victoria asked instead, looking between the two of them, suddenly a protective mother.

Agatha gulped.

This was it.

This was when they died.

“We are, mom,” Rio said softly, taking her mother’s hand in her own, willing her to be normal about this. “Agatha is it for me.”

Agatha felt her heart swell.

Agatha felt her heart explode.

Rio still loved her.

Victoria gasped, brown hair swaying as she moved her head. “Like marriage, it?”

Rio looked back and grabbed Agatha’s hand with her own. Agatha stared back, eyes watering. “Like in every way she’ll have me, it.”

Fuck, she should have bought that ring.

She would have gotten down on one knee at that moment.

Agatha smiled back, big and watery and deep.

I love you too, she wanted it to say. I love you too.

“Your father cheated on me,” Victoria said suddenly, almost a proclamation.

Agatha gasped.

“Victoria, I’m so sorry,” she began, but Rio patted her leg, shaking her head slowly.

“With what, mother?” Rio said calmly. “A real person, this time?”

Victoria clutched her chest dramatically, “Obviously.”

“Forgive me for questioning. Last time, it was with a cheese grater. And did they have sex?”

Victoria was suspiciously quiet. “Your father doesn’t love me anymore,” she announced, getting up and pacing the room. “He’s cheating on me, I know it.”

Agatha eyed her wearily.

“You told me you don’t love him, like, when I was six,” Rio muttered, crossing her arms. “Why do you care?”

“That’s not the point,” Victoria said, threading her hands through her hair. “He doesn’t get to screw me over and move on.”

“As far as I understand, he has screwed no one.”

“You’re just your father’s little bitch, aren’t you?” Victoria spat.

Agatha flinched at the comment, rage building in her, arm flying to Rio’s leg.

But Rio seemed… unbothered.

“My relationship with him does not mean I love you any less, mom. But you do see that you’re being irrational.”

Agatha couldn’t help it, but she flinched.

How was Rio so… distant?

“Irrational?” Victoria roared. “How am I being irrational?”

“Did you even try to talk to him? Or did you listen to half a fucking sentence and jump the gun?”

Agatha’s entire world stilled.

A throwaway comment.

Nothing to note.

Except this is exactly what Agatha did, didn’t she?

Did you even try to talk to him?

Tell Rio we are done. I don’t want to see her face ever again.

Or did you listen to half a fucking sentence and jump the gun?

I don’t want you in my life. I want you to leave me alone.

It was stupid, irrational, but deep down, it felt like Rio was talking to her.

I never want to see your face again.

She knows it was crazy.

She knows it was wrong.

But it almost felt as if she saw herself in Victoria.

In the way she carried herself.

In the way she jumped to conclusions.

In the way she talked to Rio.

She knew it was crazy, she did.

But she believed it anyway.

Did you even try to talk to him? Or did you listen to half a fucking sentence and jump the gun?

The words Rio so casually flung at her mother, was everything Agatha was scared she would realize.

Maybe she already had.

Maybe she had already picked up on Agatha’s worst habit.

I don’t want you here.

She wants to say she didn’t know where all this came from.

I don’t want you in my life.

But she did.

I want you to leave me alone.

The one thing Agatha could always count on was her ability to self-destruct.

I never want to see your face again.

Her ability to take something pretty sitting in the palm of her hand and crush it.

Have your stuff out of my house before I come back.

“Why can’t you just tell me I’m right? Why do you always have to give me solutions?” Victoria thundered in the background, voice already dangerously muffled as Agatha tried to breathe. “Why can’t you just hold my hand and tell me it will all be okay?”

Yes, yes, why can’t you Rio?

Why can’t you help me?

I’m broken.

I’m defective.

I’m unhappy and evil and undeserving.

“I’m your daughter, not your spouse. Call Dad,” Rio said, quite dismissively.

Rio didn’t care.

Rio wouldn’t understand.

She was broken beyond repair.

She had to protect Rio.

She had to protect her from herself.

Did you listen to half a fucking sentence and jump the gun?

Because that is what she did, didn’t she?

She threw a live grenade into the situation before the other person could even try to talk.

She hit them where it hurt.

She destroyed them from within.

Because deep down, deep down there was a part of her that believed she was evil. Bad. Unloveable.

I don’t think I am enough either. I don’t think I am good. I don’t think I get to be happy.

I don’t think I get to be happy.

I don’t think I get to be happy.

She knew it in her soul. She knew the other shoe would drop.

She should just urge it along.

Why spend years with Rio? Better to know now, right.

Better to know before she does something stupid and buys a ring.

Better to know before she was stupid and caught unaware.

The door slammed.

“What the hell just happened,” Agatha whispered behind her.

Rio sighed again. “Ladies and Gentlemen,” Rio announced, gesturing to the closed guest room door. “Victoria Vidal.”

How did Rio still not see it?

“No, Rio,” Agatha’s voice was shaking. “Why the hell did you behave like that?”

“Like what?” Rio said, defenses rising.

“Like she was insane,” Agatha waved her hands wildly.

Like I was insane.

“Because she is,” Rio sighed.

No, no, no.

“You were so dismissive of her, so cold towards her,” Agatha whispered, voice raw.

Are you going to be like that towards me?

When we get married, are you going to be that way towards me?

“You don’t understand, Agatha,” Rio pressed her temples, squeezing her eyes shut. “This is how she is, like fucking whiplash. I don’t have time for this shit in my life.”

Fuck, fuck, fuck.

Is that what Rio thought she was?

Whiplash?

“You’re shutting her out,” Agatha almost cried, “Just like you shut me out earlier.”

“How is this about you?” Rio grouched, “When did this become about us?”

Isn’t it?

Hasn’t it always been?

In this light, Rio almost looked like someone she was always running away from, someone with the same cold touch and dismissive tone.

No.

No.

But on some level, so true.

“I knew you there was something I was missing,” Agatha said, threading her hands through her hair, “I knew the other shoe would drop.”

Rio was so much like her mother.

Rio would start hating her too.

It was too perfect.

She was never meant to be happy.

“What other shoe?” Rio snapped, “What the hell are you talking about?”

“You’re emotionally avoidant, Rio. Fully fucking detached. You don’t care. You don’t care about your mother or about me or my feelings—”

“I don’t care?” Rio growled. “You can’t say that to me, Agatha. After everything we have… You don’t get to—”

How didn’t she see it before?

How didn’t she see through all of this before?

“This was all an act, wasn’t it,” Agatha’s voice rose, “You being this perfect girlfriend, doting on me, taking care of me, this was all an act.”

Rio reeled back, gasping almost as if Agatha had physically slapped her.

In some ways, she had.

“I need to go,” Rio said, heart beating wildly. “I need to go.”

Of course, Agatha wasn’t going to get a conversation.

Of course, Rio was just going to run away.

Of course, this was going to end just like Agatha knew it would.

She wanted to hate Rio at that moment.

But all she hated was herself.

As she stared at the door, slam still thundering through the room, all she could feel was intense amounts of self-loathing.

Because the one thing Agatha could always count on was her ability to self-destruct.

I never want to see your face again.

Her torturous ability to take something pretty sitting in the palm of her hand and crush it.

I don’t want you here. I don’t want you in my life.

This is how it always ended.

Because somewhere deep within her, she knew her mother was right.

She was evil.

She was rotten.

She was unloveable.

I don’t think I get to be happy.

I don’t think I get to be happy.

I don’t think I get to be happy.

She knew it in her soul.

And she would have believed it all too.

If she didn’t walk into their room and see Scratchy in his cage, eating a special treat Rio had so painstakingly made for him.

If she didn’t see the little post-it Rio had left for her on the vanity mirror earlier that morning.

Hope you aren’t questioning the universe, today. I love you <3

If she wasn’t literally ring shopping that morning.

If every single part of her didn’t fully know she loved Rio.

Fuck.

Fuck.

Fuck.

She was a fucking idiot.

What was she thinking?

Why did she do this?

She needed to find Rio.

She needed to run after her.

She needed to fix this.

She didn’t even know how she was outside, her legs carried her long before her mind accepted it, running outside, air hitting her face, looking wildly around for any hint of where she would have gone.

Fuck, she should have called her.

Rio could be anywhere right now.

Where’s her phone, where’s her keys—

Rio was in the car.

In the driveway.

She was still here?

She stayed?

Agatha didn’t know if she should go in, she didn’t know if Rio would still want to see her.

But she had to try to fix this.

Agatha slipped into the car silently.

Rio stared ahead, hands on the wheel unmoving.

Agatha raced through all the different things she wanted to say to Rio, but her courage never arrived to open her mouth.

Eventually, Rio murmured, “I’m going to say something, and I need you to not be mad at me after.”

Agatha took a deep breath.

Was this it?

Was this the end?

She nodded, pulling one of her legs up to her chest and hugging it close to her chest.

“I think you’re being irrational.”

Agatha sighed, dropping her head to her knee.

She was, wasn’t she?

Rio stiffened, “You promised you wouldn’t get mad at me.”

Agatha let out a laugh, watery and deep.

“You’re right,” she mumbled. “I am being irrational.”

Rio blinked against the darkness.

“You are… I just can’t understand why,” Rio said softly. “Why would you take her side after she called our relationship unnatural and told us no one would show up to the wedding and told me I should have been a still born.”

“Because— she what?” Agatha screeched.

When the living fuck did Victoria say all that?

Rio just stared at her, eyebrow raised. “Did you not hear that part?”

Absolutely fucking not, she did not.

Agatha shook her head. Disgust, rage and hatred bubbling within her with vitriol.

“I’m going to murder your mother,” Agatha growled, but Rio reached out and grabbed her hand before she could make any real effort to move.

“Can we talk first?” Rio said softly. “Please?”

Agatha laid her hand over Rio’s, lip quivering.

“I understand if you want to break up with me,” Agatha started, emotion choking her voice.

Rio blinked again. “Agatha, what?”

“I know I fucked up, I shouldn’t have said what I did… I’ll understand if you don’t want me anymore,” Agatha blurted, trying to keep her tears at bay.

Rio tilted her head. “Do you think my love is so fickle that one fight is going to break it?”

Agatha stared at her, breaths uneven.

Rio was looking at her with so much love, so much devotion.

She shook her head.

She wanted to believe it, but her body was still wracked with the memory of her doubts.

“I have spent the last ten years loving you, Agatha,” Rio reached out to cup her face. “I know you, I know you well. I was there when you broke up with Wanda and you tried to shove your tongue down my throat to make her jealous. I was there when you chose to tell me you love me two days after I got a girlfriend—”

Agatha’s defenses shot up. “That’s not my—”

“Agatha,” Rio urged her softly. “It took a lot for me to muster up the courage to say this. I don’t… I usually need space after things like this. But I know you won’t sleep if we don’t at least start talking this through, so please, let me say my part.”

Agatha whimpered under the weight of her words, nodding quickly.

“I know that you have the tendency to self-destruct, I know you do, but I also know it comes off the back of something that’s eating you up inside. I don’t know what it is, but I can make a good guess. You— you don’t have to tell me, I just— did I do something wrong? Over the last… two months we have been together, did I not show you how much I loved you every day? Where did I leave space for doubt?”

Agatha squeezed her eyes shut. “You didn’t,” she mumbled, leaning into Rio’s touch. “I just… I don’t think… It was all too perfect. You were perfect. I guess,” Agatha’s voice cracked under the weight of the emotion she had been unknowingly carrying, “I guess I just was waiting for the other shoe to drop. For you to realize that I am not worthy of you.”

Rio traced her thumb along her face. “Here I was thinking I wasn’t worthy of you.”

Agatha’s eyes shot up, surprise on the tip of her tongue, “You are Rio. Why would you think otherwise? You’ve been the best girlfriend, the best partner. You hear me, you anticipate my needs, you love me for who I am, I couldn’t ask for anything more.”

“Neither could I,” Rio’s eyes shone, “I don’t know why you can’t see it. Why can't you see how wonderful you are? How caring and loving and dependable you are?”

Agatha was silent. “I don’t know,” she muttered eventually, “I think I’m broken inside.”

Rio sighed. “I don’t think you’re broken, Agatha. I think you feel like you have to hold the weight of the world on your own. But I am here… I’m here telling you… no, asking you, begging you to let me carry some of it too.”

Agatha let out a shaky breath, tears falling free of her eyes. “I don’t know how to do that, Rio. I don’t know how to turn my mind off. It’s always yelling something at me, telling me you don’t want to hear what I want to say, telling me I’m burdening you with something you don’t need.”

Rio paused, considering her words. “I know it’s hard, but you need to talk to me. I can’t read your mind. I— You… You need to talk to me. We aren’t partners if we don’t do this together.”

Agatha nodded, letting out a watery laugh. “You’re right. You’re right. When did you get so wise?”

Rio was silent, staring at her with a tenderness Agatha reveled in, before she said, “When you got hurt…” Rio took a shaky breath, “When you got hurt, I promised myself I would try to be worthy of you. Up until that point, I thought I hadn’t been. So, everyday, I think, what would make me worthy of Agatha. A Rio worthy of you would communicate, so I tried to do that right now.”

Agatha reached forward and cupped her face. “Thank you. Thank you for staying. Thank you for talking to me. I needed this. I know… I know you process things... later.”

Rio chuckled grimly, “I do.” A sigh. “I’ll be honest, I got into the car and I was ready to drive away but I couldn’t start the car. I couldn’t drive away. Because the only person I wanted to run to was you. The only person I want to talk to when my life is falling apart is you.”

Agatha’s breath hitched as Rio’s words flooded through her.

She really was an idiot.

How could she ever think that Rio would abandon her?

When Rio was sitting here, fighting every impulse, trying to make sure Agatha was okay, how could she even think…

How could she even think that they weren’t it for each other?

After months of consistent affirmation.

After so much love and care and sheer devotion shown by Rio.

How could she?

And in the face of so much honesty, what could she do but rip her own heart open?

“I’m scared you’re only with me because of the accident,” Agatha blurted out. “I’m scared it’s because I got hurt that you figured it out, but I’m even more scared that it’s guilt. Like some fucked up reason that you think you need to take care of me. I know it’s irrational and insane, but it’s scary. Things have been too perfect. And perfect things don’t happen to me…” Agatha squeezed her eyes shut, dropping her head into her folded legs. “I’m sorry, I know I must sound batshit crazy…”

“You’re not crazy to me,” Rio whispered, soft and loud at the same time. “I understand. I understand this feeling. God, trust me I do. But you need to know, I almost hung up on the hospital twice.”

Agatha furrowed her brow. “What do you mean?”

“I had a panic attack. That day. Jen’s brunch. I started imagining a family with you and I spiraled. Nat calmed me down and then told me that there was no point in us having a relationship when I was so clearly in love with someone else. I kept declining the hospital’s call because I was trying to call you, trying to find you so I could tell you I loved you.”

Agatha felt all the air drain out of her body. In the same breath, she felt it fill with love.

“You wanted me before the accident?”

Rio leaned forward and pressed their foreheads together. “I wanted you the moment I met you.”

Agatha sighed. “I wanted you the moment I met you.”

“We’re idiots,” Rio laughed.

Agatha opened the car door and ran to the other side, opening the door for Rio. Rio awkwardly climbed out and Agatha took her into her arms, embracing her fiercely, cradling her head in her arms, holding onto her like she was Agatha’s lifeline.

Because in every way, she was.

“I know we have a lot more to talk about,” Agatha murmured into her neck, “But I needed this. I needed to know that you still loved me.”

Rio held her tighter, melting into the embrace. “I needed it too. I am still processing my feelings about what you said tonight… I need some time with that.”

Agatha let out a shaky breath. “Take all the time you need, my love. I’m not going to rush you.”

“Thank you,” Rio pressed a kiss onto her shoulder. “Until my mom leaves, can we be a united front?”

Agatha nodded into her neck. “We are a united front. We’ll just have strategy meetings after that invasion ends.”

Rio laughed into her hair. “Deal. You promise you’ll keep talking to me?”

Agatha nodded solemnly. “I do. I promise. Do you promise you’ll keep talking to me?”

Rio gasped softly, “I do.”

They held each other in the faint glow of the porch light for what seemed like forever.

For a little bit, Agatha felt the world become lighter.

Tomorrow, she will have to wake up and deal with the aftermath.

But right now, standing in Rio’s arms, hanging onto each other like they were each other’s salvation, it felt like the sun was rising after a long dark night.

It was everything she never knew she could have.

Trust. Stability. Honesty.

And slowly she began considering the possibility that maybe Rio was right.

Maybe she was enough.

Chapter 25

Chapter Summary

sometimes in the aftermath, there is another storm.

tw: approach carefully if you have mommy/ daddy issues. if you have both, read with both eyes closed.

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio Vidal woke up to a very angry rabbit.

Scratchy was on her chest, chewing on her hair, silently seething.

“Uhhhh,” Rio groaned. “Scratchy, you okay there bud?”

Scratchy wrinkled his nose in rage and, honest to God, growled at her.

Rio tried lifting him up but he snapped at her hand.

“Agathaaa,” Rio cried out, staring at the bunny in pure terror. “Our baby is trying to murder me.”

The door quickly opened and Agatha stumbled in, wearing her bright pink ‘Kiss the Chef’ apron, hair all tied up, flour on her cheek.

“What happened?” she panted, clutching her knees. “Are you okay?”

Rio pointed at the rabbit seething on her chest.

“Uh, just a slight suspicion, but I think our son is mad at us.”

Agatha breathed a sigh of relief. “Oh, thank god,” she approached the two of them, wiping her hands on her apron. “Fuck Rio, all I heard was Agatha and murder and I thought someone had broken in.”

Agatha easily scooped up the bunny.

And the traitor let her. Without a single huff.

Un-fucking-fair.

Rio grumbled and stumbled out of bed, rubbing her eyes.

“How’s my baby this morning,” Agatha cooed.

“I’m okay,” Rio groaned. Then, she looked up at Agatha who had paused mid-belly rub, Scratchy still tucked in her arms, a look of guilt flashing across her face.

“You were talking to Scratchy, weren’t you?” Rio pouted.

“You’re both my babies,” Agatha tried pacifying, but Rio was already stomping towards the bathroom.

“I can’t believe this is what it’s come to,” Rio whined as she put toothpaste on her toothbrush. “I’m displaced by a rabbit.”

“Baby, he’s yours, too,” Agatha called out behind her, shuffling in the room.

Rio heard Scratchy’s cage being bolted shut.

“I think he’s just feeling a little neglected,” Agatha said, appearing in the bathroom doorway.

Rio scoffed as she spit out the toothpaste.

“Neglected,” Rio rolled her eyes. “He literally sleeps between us most nights.”

Agatha dissolved into a sweet smile, coming up behind Rio and sliding her arms around her waist.

“We have been having a lot of sex these last few days,” Agatha murmured, kissing her shoulder. “I think he just misses his Mami.”

Rio hummed and leaned into her touch. “He’s spoiled.”

Agatha nuzzled her neck. “He’s just the beginning.”

Rio scrunched her brow. “What do you mean?”

Agatha kissed her cheek. “What do you think happens when we start this family you keep hinting at?”

Rio broke into a giant smile.

“Family, huh?” she said, spinning in Agatha’s arms.

Agatha nodded, suddenly shy. “I want to think about the future if you want to,” she mumbled, playing with the ends of Rio’s hair. “But only if you think we’re ready—”

Rio leaned in and kissed her.

Partially to shut her up.

But mainly because it was finally happening.

It was all finally falling together.

She and Agatha were going to have the most beautiful kids.

They would have Rio’s smile and Agatha’s nose and wear stubbornness like an overcoat.

“Are you sure?” Agatha asked, pulling back to search Rio’s face. “There were a lot of heavy emotions last night and I don’t blame you—”

“Don’t,” Rio said.

It was all Rio could say.

Let it stay buried.

Let it stay done.

Don’t break it open, just yet.

Agatha nodded softly, flashing a small smile, one that did not reach her eyes.

“I made—”

Rio grabbed her face and kissed her again, deep and long, hoping that the apology on her lips would make it to Agatha’s heart.

Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio’s waist, holding onto her as if she was lost at sea and Rio a lone buoy in shark-infested waters.

And Rio clung further, because Agatha was the key to her absolution, the only way she was going to make it out of this mess alive.

When they finally surfaced, Rio could see Agatha’s heart had calmed a little.

Her breaths were more even, her smile more warm.

“How do you always know what I need?” Agatha almost choked out, burrowing further into Rio’s arms. “How do you know what I need before I even know?”

“Because I love you,” Rio murmured against her forehead. “And I know you better than anyone else.”

“That you do,” Agatha said, kissing her on the cheek. “I made breakfast.”

Rio pulled back a little so she could look Agatha in the eyes. “You made breakfast?”

“Oh, don’t sound so surprised,” Agatha huffed.

“What did you break? Or maim? Or steal?” Rio teased.

“I hate you,” Agatha grumbled, but leaned in for another kiss anyway.

Rio grinned against her lips. “Did you make pancakes?”

“Maybe,” Agatha blushed.

Rio giggled as she stripped off her pajamas and bolted into the shower, the water hissing as it turned on. “Oh, I love guilt pancakes— Baby, come in quickly!”

Agatha poked her head into the shower, fully clothed. “I had a shower already— oh, don’t look at me like that.”

“You hate me,” Rio pouted.

Agatha softened. “I love you so much, baby,” she mumbled as she leaned into the shower, still fully clothed, trying to dodge the water.

Rio met her in the middle for a kiss. “If you loved me, you would come into the shower.”

Agatha looked so torn.

But she composed herself, leaned in and kissed Rio again, the tips of her hair and the edge of her shirt getting wet under the spray. “I can’t, but come to the kitchen when you’re done, I have something for you.”

“Okay,” Rio mumbled against her lips. “You’re really going to give up showering with your very naked girlfriend? Especially when she will let you do whatever you want to her?”

Agatha sighed, and pulled back, hovering near the entrance of the shower. “Baby, your mom is still here.”

And suddenly it all crashed into her, a tidal wave of suppressed emotions.

What you two are doing is unnatural, you know that?

You can’t get married, no one will show up.

My mother was right, you are unnatural.

You were a still born, you should have stayed that way.

From now, you won’t have a mother.

All she could think about was a house but not a home, of too much anger in the silences, of lives lived separately, out of sync, in spite and loss and hatred. A life where she might end up looking at Agatha one day and finding that she didn’t look at Rio with any love anymore, with any happiness anymore—

“Breathe in.”

Something was cupping her cheek.

Agatha was cupping her cheek.

Agatha was there.

“Breathe out.”

There was a hand on her chest, pressing softly above her heart.

Agatha brought Rio’s hand to her own chest, holding it there so Rio could feel her heart beat.

“Focus on my heartbeat, baby.”

Thump, thump, thump.

Soft, gentle, kind.

And present.

“Focus on it, my love,” Agatha was saying in the distance, but it was muffled. “And we breathe in,” Agatha took a deep breath, her chest rising. Rio followed, air flowing into her lungs with such force she almost fell to the ground.

Wait, she was already on the ground.

How did she get here?

“Okay, good,” Agatha mumbled. “Now tell me five things you can see.”

“What?” Rio choked out, but her voice came out hoarse and raw.

“Five things you can see around you,” Agatha urged.

Rio looked around the shower in a daze. The shower was still running, everything was blurry and messy and a daze.

But Agatha wanted her to do something.

So, Rio was going to try.

“I see a shower head, uh, the door, um, the soap, your pink apron, and you.”

Agatha smiled and nodded.

“Good, my love. Now four things you can touch.”

“Touch?” Rio stuttered.

The world felt liquid in this moment, soupy, molten.

“Yes, what are four things you can touch? How do they feel?”

Rio moved her thumb slowly where it rested against Agatha’s chest.

“I feel your blouse. It's wet.”

Agatha laughed, soft and low.

It encouraged Rio to keep speaking.

“I feel your hair. It’s thick and soft and also wet.”

Agatha took another long, deep breath, and Rio followed, air entering her lungs slowly.

“I feel the stone beneath my legs,” Rio continued, feeling the rough surface rub against her shin. “It’s hard and gritty.”

Rio wrinkled her nose. “I can’t really smell anything here. Except the water.”

Agatha nodded. “Last thing, what can you taste? Doesn’t have to be something you’re tasting right now, just imagine it, focus on it.”

Rio closed her eyes.

And all she could think about was Agatha’s lips.

So, she leaned forward and captured them.

This kiss wasn’t hurried or desperate.

It was a whisper, a promise, a routine.

One that gave Rio a glimpse into soft mornings and rainy evenings, wrapped up in Agatha’s heart, listening to her heartbeat as the world drudged on around them.

This was what she had dreamed about for the last decade. Her only shot at a happy future.

And when Agatha pulled away, she felt like she was herself again.

She could feel movement in her toes, air in her lungs, and the soft tinging of their kiss on her lips.

“Are you okay?” Agatha whispered.

Rio just stared.

The shower was still running in the distance and now Rio could see that Agatha was fully soaked, head to toe, her bright pink apron now a dark magenta.

“You’re wet,” Rio noted. “Why did you come into the shower with your clothes on?”

Agatha scrunched up her nose.

“You had a panic attack,” she said. “Nothing else mattered.”

Oh.

Rio didn’t know when she started crying, but this was definitely the moment she started bawling.

She slammed the shower knob shut and launched herself into Agatha’s arms, immediately burrowing her face in Agatha’s neck.

“You didn’t have to do that,” Rio mumbled into her neck, voice thick with emotion.

Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio’s middle and held her close to her heart. “You’re acting like you literally won’t jump into a pit of snakes for me if I asked you too.”

“It doesn’t mean you have to jump too,” Rio whispered.

“Oh but it does,” Agatha affirmed. “You jump, I jump, Jack.”

Rio wanted to laugh, but something was still pushing in on her neck, making her dizzy and light-headed.

“Agatha, you don’t have to do this. This is my family, my mess. You don’t need to fix it. Fix me.”

Agatha froze.

Rio opened her mouth to swallow her words, but Agatha beat her to it.

“Rio, last night you told me that you want to carry my share of the world. Do you still mean it?”

Rio nodded quickly.

“Then why do you think that I don’t need to reciprocate the same love you show me?”

Each word was slow, carefully chosen.

But they hit Rio with the same damning force.

“I don’t know,” was all she could say.

It was all she knew to say.

Let it go, her heart beat, hoping Agatha would hear it without the words leaving her mouth.

Don’t bring it up, please.

But Agatha had that determined look in her eye that only came when she sniffed out a lie and was hell-bent on uncovering the truth

“Does it have anything to do with…”

Her mother?

Her father?

The two bat-shit crazy people who were her parents?

“It does,” Rio mumbled, holding Agatha closer. Please don’t leave me.

Maybe if Rio held her hard enough, she wouldn’t want to leave.

“Have you ever thought of setting boundaries with them?” Agatha asked softly.

“I can’t cut them off,” Rio cried into Agatha’s neck, words pouring out of place she didn’t even know feelings could hide. “I know I have to, at the back of my head, I know I have to, but they’re my parents. For all the horrible shit they have said to me, I have also said shit back, so much shit, Agatha. I literally told my mom to kill herself when I was fourteen. I’ve said worse stuff to my dad. I know it isn’t healthy the way we exist, but,” Rio felt her voice crack, “I can’t just cut them out of my life. But I don’t know how to keep going like this. I’m scared. I’m so, so scared that we will become them.”

Agatha cupped her face, thumbs gently tracing her skin.

“I never said you have to cut them off,” Agatha pacified. “Just that you have to set some ground rules—”

“They don’t respond to ground rules,” Rio said firmly. “I learned the hard way that I just have to roll over and take it. The screaming, it’s just the way we fight. I promise you it’ll blow over. But if I try to leave, if I try to push back, it won’t go well, trust me, I’ve tried—”

“Rio, Rio, breathe in, baby.”

Agatha was breathing in with her again.

Had she talked herself into another panic attack?

By the look in Agatha’s eyes, she had.

Goddamn it, why couldn't she just handle it herself—

“Baby, this may not be the right time, but I think you need to hear this,” Agatha spoke, pulling Rio’s focus back towards her. “Love is not conditional. There is no check-list of things you have to do. There is no fixed way it will be delivered to you. You’re allowed to ask for more. You’re allowed to ask for change. It won’t go away if you ask it to come to you a little differently.”

“But it almost has,” Rio choked out. “Every time I try to fight back, my parents remind me of all they have done, of all the ways they were hurt by their parents— what do I say in the face of all that?”

“You say enough,” Agatha said firmly. “You say not anymore.”

“I can’t,” Rio breathed.

“Will you let me then?”

“No— Agatha, don’t get in the middle of this, don’t—”

But Rio stopped short.

Because Agatha looked very, very guilty.

“Oh no, what did you do—”

“I was only trying to help, promise—”

The door bell rang.

And all hell broke loose.

“Rio,” her mother banged on the bathroom door. “Why is your father here?”

“You called my father here?” Rio screeched.

“We kept in touch, I thought he would help—”

“This is the exact opposite of helping, Agatha—”

“Just let me explain—”

But Rio was already scrambling out of the shower and throwing on her discarded nightclothes to greet the absolute shit-show that was probably brewing outside.

But she opened the door to silence.

Rio bolted into the living room to find her father and mother talking… normally?

In polite, hushed tones?

Had the apocalypse descended on them?

But then Victoria reared her head, “So, this is the trick up your sleeve—”

“Victoria,” a voice cut through the room.

It wasn’t Rio’s. Wasn’t her father’s either.

Agatha stepped through the doorway of their bedroom, still sopping wet, a single sheet of paper in her hand.

“I talked about this with Bertie today, but I’m suggesting this for the both of you,” Agatha leaned forward and put a piece of paper before them.

She looked up at Rio while Victoria read the piece of paper.

“Stop me anytime,” she whispered, voice thick with unshed tears. “I’m going to try my best not to, but stop me if I cross a line.”

Rio just stared at her, heart beating wildly in her chest.

Agatha was playing a dangerous game.

And Rio didn’t want the woman she loved to get hurt.

But before Rio could even try to stop her, Agatha started talking.

“I spent all night looking into a bunch of therapy clinics in your area, and I found one with a lot of therapists that specialize in relationship and family therapy. I didn’t want to pick one for you, so, um, I paid for five sessions with the clinic. Three for couples therapy and two as an individual season, each.”

She gulped and sneaked a quick look at Rio to check in, flashed a small smile, before quickly continuing. “I can’t make you do anything, but I really hope you try. Because Victoria the way you spoke to Rio will never happen again. It was not appropriate. It was not okay.”

Agatha took a shaky breath. “And I know it’s hard to leave all your scars behind. But as someone with," Agatha's voice cracked, "not great parents, I see one very big difference here. You both seem to care enough to show up. To try. So, now what I, we, are asking from you. You can’t hide your knife behind your love anymore. It’s hurting the woman I love, so please, please, if you love your daughter, then try. Try to be better. Try to do better. And maybe along the way you’ll heal yourself too.”

The world was blurry now.

Rio was sure there were tears in her eyes.

She wanted to throw her arms around Agatha just for trying to fix this.

Just for trying to help.

But she was so scared of what was coming next.

Victoria opened her mouth.

Bertie squeezed her knee softly.

And Victoria snapped it shut.

And nodded.

Rio staggered back.

This had never happened before.

“Today was the first time in probably ten years that your father told me he still cared about me,” Victoria choked out. “I don’t know where it came from, but I didn’t know how much I missed it until now.”

Bertie let out a small scoff, but there was no anger in it, only amazement.

“Today was the first time in a long time I realized that I do still have a wife,” he nodded, looking up at Agatha. “That if I tried, I might be able to salvage this.”

“So, I would like to try,” he said, turning to Victoria. “But you have to promise me, you leave the kids out of this. This is between you and me, and if the ship sinks, so be it.”

Victoria’s lip quivered under the weight of his words.

But she still nodded.

“I’ll send you the details,” Agatha murmured and moved to walk into the room, eyes lowered, hands trembling.

Rio wanted to run after her, but her mother caught her arm.

“I’m sorry, honey,” she said, eyes filled with tears. “For whatever it’s worth.”

Rio didn’t know where it came from, but she opened her mouth, “Show me,” Rio mumbled, courage rising. “Don’t say you’re sorry, show me.”

And possibly for the second time that day, completely ruining Rio from the inside and shattering her entire worldview, Victoria just nodded.

No fireworks, no fanfare.

“Victoria, can you go grab your stuff?” Bertie asked, moving up behind her.

Victoria silently moved away, leaving Rio alone with her father.

“Dad, what the hell is going on?” Rio blurted out the second the door closed.

“Did you know you could send 20,000 characters in a single text on iMessage,” Bertie said, opening his phone, and squinting at the text.

“I—huh?”

“Because I didn’t,” he nodded, then holding up the screen toward Rio, “Until I got this message this morning.”

There was a massive gray text bubble that consumed the entire screen and then more. Bertie tapped a small ‘show more’ at the end which opened even more text which he scrolled for a good few seconds and did not reach the end.

“Agatha wrote all of that?” Rio spluttered.

“Your girlfriend writes wonderfully, by the way,” Bertie said, pulling the phone back, before Rio could actually read any of it. “Real gift.”

“She— she wrote all that?”

Bertie nodded. “Imagine me, I wake up to a very long text from my daughter’s girlfriend which starts with your wife is in our house, hope you know. I did not know, by the way. My wife flew across the country and I did not even know.”

Rio’s mind was reeling.

Her heart felt so full.

Her brain, so impossibly heavy.

“What did Agatha say?”

Bertie let out a small laugh and shook his head. “So much, trust me mija, your girlfriend did not hold back.”

He took a deep breath, placing his hand on Rio’s shoulder. “I didn’t get it the first time I read it. I got really angry, actually. I didn’t like that someone from outside our family was telling me what to do.”

But then, in a warm, almost soft voice, “But I had nothing to do on the plane. So, I read it again. The second time, I understood it a little more. By the third time, I could cede that she had a point. And by the time I landed, I felt how deeply I had failed you.”

His voice cracked at the end. Rio had never seen her father cry.

“Because Agatha was right,” he whispered, voice thick with emotion. “You have been the bandaid covering the gaping hole in our marriage. We asked you to take on the mantle of parent when you were so young. You shouldn't have— Agatha said it has a psychological name, I think, uh, parentified child...? I have it written down on my notes app. I will read about it more."

But then he cleared his throat, eyes entirely glassy. "All I am saying is I agree with her. We have put you in such an awful position, and it is not fair. I love you, Rio. You’re mi vida. My entire life. I held your little hand in mine when you were born and promised you that I would not let anyone hurt you. And then I turned around and did just that.”

He leaned forward and brushed a tear from her cheek.

“But not anymore,” he promised. “This stops with me. Your mom and I, we’re going to figure it out. We’re going to be better. I can’t promise that your mom and I will fix things overnight, but just looking at her right now, backing down when I told her I still cared, it makes me think Agatha was right about yet another thing.”

Rio let out a wet laugh. “I’ve realized she’s right about most things.”

Bertie joined in, soft, joyful laughter ringing through the room.

“Something else particular happened,” Bertie stated, looking at Rio somberly. “You know how we lost your grandmother’s ring after her funeral?”

Rio nodded, sadness pinging in her heart.

She had always loved that ring.

It had a purple garnet in the center of a beautiful diamond azalea.

Years ago, she had begged her grandmother to give her the ring, because even fresh-out-of-college Rio Vidal knew it was meant for Agatha Harkness.

But the ring had disappeared right after the funeral five years ago.

“Well,” her father said, patting around his breast pocket, “In my hurry today, I grabbed the wrong jacket from the back of the coat closet, and guess what I found.”

He pulled out the ring.

“No,” Rio gasped, grabbing it from his hands. “It can’t be.”

But Bertie just nodded enthusiastically. “Sometimes, things are just meant to be.”

Bertie kissed the top of her head.

“I know you don’t need my blessing or anything,” he said softly. “And I should probably give it to her, not you, but it’s so rare to find someone who will stick it to the world just to stand up for you. Don’t let a love like this slip from your hands.”

Rio stared at the ring in awe.

This had to be fate.

This had to be destiny.

“I won’t,” Rio murmured. “I’ve been planning a proposal for like two years.”

“Didn’t you only get together two months ago?”

Rio stared at her father with the best serious look she could muster in the face of all softness. “Yes.”

Bertie nodded, a giant smile breaking through. “I was thinking of inviting the both of you to dinner, but I think me and your mom should just go alone. Give you some time to make up properly.”

Rio shoved his shoulder.

He rubbed it in fake indignation. “You’re too big to be pushing me around. I’ll report you to your wife.”

“I’ll report you to your wife,” Rio threatened.

Bertie loosened his collar in mock horror. ‘Oh shit, mine is much scarier.”

Rio giggled with her father, feeling so damn light.

“Are you ready?” Victoria’s voice came into the room as she opened the door.

Bertie nodded, giving Rio one last kiss on her forehead, and trotted over towards their bedroom where he knocked twice.

Agatha opened the door apprehensively, now changed into dry sweatpants and a t-shirt.

“Thank you,” Bertie said before he took Agatha into a hug.

Agatha squeezed him tight and Rio could see how much it meant to her to have a parent-figure show her love.

It made Rio’s heart shatter into a million pieces.

Her parents left in a blur of quick farewells and promises to check in and suddenly the door slammed shut and it was just the two of them.

Rio could hear Agatha’s breath waver.

“I’m sorry,” she stuttered out. “I—I didn’t want to overstep, I just wanted to help—”

But Rio had already closed the distance.

She kissed Agatha like she was air.

Like she was the answer to her prayer, water after a draught, a gift bestowed upon her by a cosmic entity.

Like she was her salvation.

Because, in every single way, she was.

This weekend alone proved it.

Proved that they could handle the good with the bad.

Proved that they could do this, forever.

When they surfaced neither of them said anything.

They just stood there, foreheads pressed, in the silence of the aftermath.

Because the storm has finally passed.

But they had made it through.

“We should go check on Scratchy,” Agatha mumbled eventually. “When I was in there, he was thumping against the cage like crazy.”

Rio let out an endeared scoff. “He’s so dramatic."

“He’s our son,” Agatha affirmed as she led Rio into their room.

And as Rio walked in behind her, going into their bedroom, in their home, to their bunny, with Agatha’s engagement ring tucked safely into her pocket, she had never felt safer.

Never felt happier.

Now all she had to do was keep her big mouth shut and not get on one knee until the time was right.

How hard could it be?

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha Harkness was expecting some kind of blow up.

She had probably crossed like seventeen lines in the last thirty minutes.

As she paced in the room, trying to give Rio and her parents some space after basically forcing therapy down their throats, she tried her best to not burst into tears.

Because she just wanted to help.

And by the look on Rio’s face when she found out Agatha had texted her father, she did not help.

Scratchy thumped softly against the cage again and again, trying to get her attention, but she was too focused on the soft laughter ringing through the closed door.

That was a good sign, right?

Right?

Agatha was now very, very close to tears.

She didn’t mean to throw a live grenade into Rio’s life.

She didn’t mean to cause pain.

She had good intentions.

Fuck, she was doing it again, she was making it all about her—

There was a knock at the door.

Agatha quickly moved to open it and saw Bertie on the other end, eyes warm and amused.

“Thank you,” he said simply, and moved to give her the biggest hug.

Agatha burrowed into it, so fucking glad she hadn’t entirely destroyed Rio’s life.

And a small part of her broke and healed in this hug, at the non-transactional show of appreciation from a paternal figure.

She had never had that before.

Bertie softly whispered in her ear before they pulled away, “Remember what I said, okay? Don’t wait too long for the next step.”

Agatha’s eyes widened and when she pulled back there was a teasing gleam in Bertie’s eyes.

Next step.

Would they even make it?

Agatha still blushed and stepped back, rubbing her chest to ease the sinking feeling in her chest.

Because when all was said and done, and the door slammed shut, Agatha couldn’t help but want to spiral all over again.

She expected, actually, no, deserved, Rio to tell her off, or seethe, maybe even yell.

But the last thing she expected Rio to do was jump into her arms and kiss her like she was everything.

Rio had actually been doing a lot of that today.

Shutting Agatha up with her lips.

Agatha should have been ashamed by how easily it fucking worked.

But she wasn’t.

She couldn’t help but bask in the warmth that came from Rio’s lips, the way she held her waist and tried to absorb her into her heart.

But she knew they had a lot more talking to do.

Unfortunately for her, Rio did not seem to share that idea.

“I can’t believe you did that,” Rio murmured against her lips as they pulled apart to take a few shaky breaths.

“I thought you would be mad—”
