Rio was really coming at her as if she was a woman starved.

And Agatha would have been really into it if they weren’t carrying the weight of an important conversation on their back.

“Baby,” she panted when she pulled back. “We need to talk.”

“Later,” Rio mumbled, trying to pull her back in.

Agatha was not strong enough.

But as Rio’s hands trembled against her skin, she realized that this was another way Rio was running from something she didn’t want to say.

And she realized, in that moment, that maybe she needed to be strong enough for both of them.

“I’m scared,” Agatha blurted out as they rose for another round of air. “I am so scared.”

Rio stilled, arms dropping from their place under Agatha’s shirt as she pulled back.

“I’m scared, too,” she mumbled, lip quivering.

“Do you want to talk about it,” Agatha asked, already hating the way Rio seemed so broken.

Rio squeezed her eyes shut, but nodded anyway.

“I, uh, don’t know where to start,” she whispered, eyes tracing the ground.

Oh, my love.

“Come here,” Agatha said, reaching out to take her hand and leading her towards their bed. She sat down, legs crossed on the covers and Rio did the same.

They were facing each other, fingers still intertwined, but Rio was still looking down, looking away.

“I love you,” Rio mumbled, her finger traced a pattern into the duvet.

“I love you, too,” Agatha affirmed, squeezing her hand. “You don’t have to talk about anything you don’t have to.”

“I know,” Rio whispered, squeezing her eyes shut. “Can I ask you a question?”

“Of course, baby.”

Rio took a deep breath, a sliver of a smile shining through. “What did you write to my Dad?”

Agatha never had a greater urge to crawl into a hole and die.

“Uh, just a little something,” she mumbled, rubbing her neck.

“I thought we were being honest here,” Rio raised her brow. “Where did all of this come from Agatha?”

Agatha sighed deeply and shook her head.

“You’re not allowed to make fun of me for this,” she threatened.

Rio tilted her head in confusion but nodded anyway.

“Okay, sometimes, only when I am really, really confused,” Agatha took a deep breath. “Sometimes I go on… Reddit.”

Rio gulped, eyes wide and then burst into laughter.

“You promised you wouldn’t make fun of me for this!” Agatha whined, snatching her hand from Rio’s and crossing her arms.

Rio squeezed her lips shut and tried to compose herself.

Agatha pouted, but continued, “I, sometimes, log into Reddit just to get advice on things I can’t ask people in real life about… stop laughing.”

A snicker escaped before Rio composed herself.

“I’m sorry, I’m sorry. Continue.”

“Last night, I couldn’t sleep because, well, everything that happened…” Agatha sighed again, squeezing her eyes shut.

Suddenly, Rio wasn’t laughing anymore.

She reached forward and grabbed Agatha’s hand again, squeezing it softly.

“I, uh, asked for advice on what to do. I— I didn’t mention any details, promise. Just that your mom said some horrible things and how guilty I felt for making it worse.”

Agatha took a deep breath, tears pricking her eyes.

“What did Reddit say?” Rio asked softly.

“Someone on Reddit told me to write it all out. Like just get all my feelings down on paper and sometimes it helps to write it like a letter and before I knew it I was writing a letter to your dad. I don’t know why… actually I do know why. He’s probably the only parental figure I’ve kept in touch with…”

“You kept in touch with my Dad?” Rio asked, eyes wide.

Agatha gulped. “Uh, he sends me birthday wishes on Facebook and I keep him updated on the big milestones and stuff, and, uh, sometimes we text each other to check in on you.

Rio looked like her brain was caving in.

“He even texted me when we got together,” Agatha blurted out.

“He did?” Rio blinked, bewildered.

Agatha nodded, a soft smile setting on her lips. “He did. He said something sweet too… wait, let me find it.”

Agatha pulled out her phone and scrolled past the insanely long ramble she had sent Rio’s dad as fast as she could before finding the messages from two months ago.

“He said, thank god you two finally saw what we’ve been seeing for a decade. Please don’t wait this long before the wedding.”

“He did not say that,” Rio groaned, grabbing the phone from her hand and reading his texts. “Wow, he is not subtle at all.”

Agatha tilted her head. “What does that mean?”

“Uh, nothing,” Rio said far too quickly.

Agatha pouted again. “Honesty goes both ways.”

“Trust me,” Rio shook her head. “If I tell you what I am thinking right now, you will murder me.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes, but let the discussion drop.

Instead, she picked up a far more lethal thread.

“Do you think we’re moving too fast?”

Rio blinked into the silence as the question rolled over her.

“Too fast?” she spluttered. “Do you think we’re moving too fast?”

Agatha rubbed her temple, “I—I don’t know. I want to marry you like now, I want to have your adorable, stubborn children, but it’s only been two months, Rio. You’ve had foot fungus for longer than that. Am I crazy?”

“You’re not crazy,” Rio said softly, cupping Agatha’s cheek. “You’re not crazy because I want it too.”

“You do?”

“You know I do,” Rio smiled, a tease creeping through the softness. “I think I’ve been very clear about how much I want you. How much I want a future with you.”

Agatha looked down, lower lip trembling. “I know, but I don’t want to rush this. I don’t want to fuck it up because we are going too fast.”

“We’re ten years in the making, Agatha,” Rio gently brushed her thumb along her face. “We have ten years worth of knowing each other—of loving each other— under our belt. Two months is crazy for strangers. But you and I, we were always destined to end up here. From the moment I met you, there could never be anyone else.”
